# 13.19. OVN pipeline stage catalog (63 stage full 20-axis)

> **State:** This part is a cross-reference catalog of 63 stages (28 LS_IN + 11 LS_OUT + 19 LR_IN + 6 LR_OUT) keyed against Part 13.16 (table ID map) and Part 13.17 (register convention).
> **Presentation purpose:** each cornerstone stage gets its own section with the 20-axis natural treatment (concept, history, position, role, motivation, problems, importance, mechanism, operator mastery, classification, workflow, incident, tightly related, version differences, observation, source code, real-world incident, synthetic exercise, common failures, comparison with other systems). Secondary stages are gathered at the end of the part.
> **Language status:** Mixed. Header through §13.19.12 are now English. The remaining sections (§13.19.13 onward) will be translated by sister agents under plan v3.12.

## Learning objectives

After this part, the learner can:

1. For each pipeline stage, state the table number on `br-int`, the role, and the `REGBIT`/`MLF` bits that it sets or clears.
2. Trace a packet through the pipeline with `ovn-trace` and identify the stage that drops the packet.
3. Debug stage misbehavior with `lflow-list` and `ovn-detrace` cookie reverse lookup.

## Prerequisites

- Part 13.8 (ovn-northd compile), Part 13.16 (pipeline IDs map), Part 13.17 (register convention).

## Pipeline structure

| Pipeline | Stage count | Stage tier |
|----------|-------------|-------------|
| Logical Switch IN (LS_IN) | 28 stages | 6 core + 10 supporting + 12 peripheral |
| Logical Switch OUT (LS_OUT) | 11 stages | 5 supporting + 6 peripheral |
| Logical Router IN (LR_IN) | 19 stages | 4 core + 4 supporting + 11 peripheral |
| Logical Router OUT (LR_OUT) | 6 stages | 1 supporting + 5 peripheral |

Verified against `northd/northd.c` `PIPELINE_STAGES` on branch-22.03 in Part 13.16: 63 actual stages (not 64 as the REF document claims).

---

## §13.19.1 LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2: the L2 spoofing filter at the head of the pipeline

**Concept.** `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` is logical stage **number 0** of the ingress pipeline on a `Logical_Switch`. Every packet entering the LS must pass through it first. The stage has two interleaved responsibilities. First, drop a packet whose `eth.src` is not in the `Logical_Switch_Port.port_security` set (this stops MAC spoofing at L2). Second, drop, with delay, any packet that the `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_IP` or `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_ND` stage marked on `REGBIT_PORT_SEC_DROP` for IP, ARP, or ND spoofing. On `br-int`, this stage maps to OF table 8 (using the formula `8 + logical_table` from Part 13.16). Type: a core pipeline stage, sub-type "ingress security gate".

**History and background.** The stage has existed since OVN 2.4 (2015), when Bryant and Pettit ported NSX port-security into OVN. The first version only checked `eth.src`. OVN 20.06 (2020) split port-security into three sequential stages (`L2`, `IP`, `ND`) and introduced the "deferred drop" pattern via `REGBIT_PORT_SEC_DROP`, so that IP and ND failures still use the shared `drop` instruction in the final L2 stage. Funneling all drop points to one place makes drop-counter accounting easier. OVN 21.03 added support for multicast MAC entries inside `port_security`.

**Position in the architecture.** Logical stage 0 maps to OF table 8 (`8 + 0`). This is the **first** flow that ovn-controller installs on `br-int` for any ingress packet coming from a tap port (vif). There is no OVN pipeline before this stage. The only thing that comes before is OF table 0, which OVN installs to map the vif port number to a datapath: it sets `metadata = datapath.tunnel_key`, `reg14 = inport.tunnel_key`, and then runs `goto_table 8`. Scope: per-packet, per-LSP.

**Role.** Primary role: **L2 anti-spoofing gatekeeper**. Secondary role: **drop sink** for any packet that an earlier stage flagged with `REGBIT_PORT_SEC_DROP`. If you disable this stage, a tenant can forge the MAC of another VM on the same LS (lateral spoofing). Influence scope: one inbound packet at a time, with no state retained after the stage.

**Why it exists.** Before OVN, NSX-V used the ESXi vSwitch with the `dvfilter` feature to block MAC spoofing. When OVN was created to provide multi-tenant L2 abstraction on Linux KVM, port-security became a must-have, because the Linux kernel hypervisor does not block MAC spoofing on a tap interface by default (the tap driver does not check the source MAC). Without it, a tenant who compromises a VM could forge the gateway MAC, poison the ARP cache of every VM in the same subnet, and run a man-in-the-middle attack. This stage closes that gap at the OVN logical layer.

**Problems it solves.** Specifically, MAC spoofing at the tap port: a VM sends a packet whose `eth.src` does not match a MAC declared when its `Logical_Switch_Port.addresses` was created. The fix: ovn-northd compiles the `Logical_Switch_Port.port_security` list (the allowed MAC list) into a Logical_Flow at priority 50 that matches `inport == "lsp1" && eth.src == {AA:BB:CC:DD:EE:01, AA:BB:CC:DD:EE:02}` with action `next`, plus a priority-0 fallback `drop` for any packet that does not match. Scope: only L2 spoofing. IP and ARP spoofing are handled by two separate stages (`PORT_SEC_IP`, `PORT_SEC_ND`) that route their drops back here for the shared drop instruction.

**Importance.** A central pipeline stage. Every ingress packet traverses it, and every `Logical_Switch` has it. If the stage is misconfigured (an empty `port_security`), the entire tenant security model collapses. The engineer must know the exact OF table id (table 8), the match shape, and the deferred-drop semantics of `REGBIT_PORT_SEC_DROP`. Without understanding this stage one cannot debug the class of bug "VM A pings VM B but tcpdump shows a MAC anomaly".

**How it works.** Logical_Flow rows are emitted by `build_lswitch_input_port_sec_op` (`northd/northd.c:5615` at v22.03.8) and the per-datapath helper `build_lswitch_input_port_sec_od` (`northd/northd.c:5666`). The `_l2` / `_ip` / `_nd` suffix split landed in branch-24.03+; at v22.03.8 the L2, IP, and ND port-security flow generation share these two functions. Template:

```
table=0 (ls_in_port_sec_l2), priority=50,
  match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == {AA:BB:CC:DD:EE:01}),
  action=(next;)

table=0 (ls_in_port_sec_l2), priority=0,
  match=(1),
  action=(drop;)
```

When the downstream IP or ND stage detects an IP spoof, it sets `reg0[0] = 1` (`REGBIT_PORT_SEC_DROP`) and still calls `next;`. At the end of the LS_IN pipeline a special flow matches `reg0[0] == 1` and drops the packet. Two paths exist (drop immediately at L2, or deferred drop through `REGBIT`), but since OVN 20.06 the REGBIT path is preferred for IP and ND, because it concentrates drop accounting in one place. Invariant: if `reg0[0] = 1` after this stage, the packet **will definitely** be dropped before it leaves LS_IN.

**How an operator masters this.** Four skills: (1) **Read**: understand that `lsp-set-port-security-addresses lsp1 "AA:BB:CC:DD:EE:01 10.0.0.5"` produces entries for both the MAC filter and the IP filter. Inspect the resulting OpenFlow with `ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=8 | grep <inport_tunnel_key>`. (2) **Modify**: use `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security-addresses lsp1 ...` and then wait for northd to finish compiling with `ovn-nbctl --wait=hv sync`. (3) **Observe**: use `ovn-trace` with a forged `eth.src` and watch which stage drops the packet. (4) **Debug**: if a user reports "VM lost connectivity after a MAC change", the reflex is to check `lsp-get-port-security` and verify whether the new MAC is in the list.

**Classification.** Stage type: **security gate** (subtype L2 anti-spoofing). Unlike `LS_IN_ACL` (policy enforcement, stateful) and `LS_IN_PRE_ACL` (state setup), this stage is purely stateless and matches only invariant packet fields (`eth.src`, `inport`).

**Usage workflow.** When configuring an LSP:
1. Create the LS and LSP: `ovn-nbctl ls-add ls1 && ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls1 lsp-vm1`.
2. Set the MAC: `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-vm1 "AA:BB:CC:DD:EE:01"`.
3. Enable port security: `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-vm1 "AA:BB:CC:DD:EE:01"`.
4. Verify: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep "ls_in_port_sec_l2"` should show two flows, one at priority 50 and one at priority 0.
5. On the hypervisor: `ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=8 | head -5` should show the corresponding rule installed.
6. Spoof test: use `scapy` to send a packet with the wrong `eth.src`. Verify that the drop counter rises with `ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=8 | grep "n_packets="`.

**When something goes wrong.** Common symptoms: (a) "A VM just restarted and cannot send any packet". Check whether the VM MAC matches `lsp-get-port-security` (cloud-init sometimes generates a random MAC if the profile is wrong). (b) "After a live migration the VM loses 30 seconds of connectivity". The cause is usually a stale ARP cache rather than this stage, but the table 8 drop counter rises and helps confirm the symptom. Cross-link: Part 20.0 §incident decision tree, Part 13.18 §REGBIT_PORT_SEC_DROP.

**Tightly related to.** Tightly coupled to: `Logical_Switch_Port.port_security` (the NBDB column that supplies the data), `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_IP` and `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_ND` (the two IP and ND stages that share the REGBIT), `REGBIT_PORT_SEC_DROP` (the deferred-drop flag), and `OFTABLE_LOG_INGRESS_PIPELINE` (the OF table family this stage belongs to). Loosely related to: the ARP cache on the VM (a higher layer), and the iptables forward chain (a lower layer outside OVN).

**Version differences.**
- OVN 2.4 (2015): a single `port_security` stage that checks `eth.src` only.
- OVN 20.06 (2020): split into three stages (`L2`, `IP`, `ND`) with the `REGBIT_PORT_SEC_DROP` deferred-drop pattern.
- OVN 21.03 (2021): adds multicast MAC entries in `port_security`.
- OVN 22.03 (2022): allows the `unknown` keyword in addresses, which disables port-security for debugging.
- OVN 24.03 (2024): a compile-time optimization that reduces the number of flows when an LSP has more than 100 MACs (rare but possible).

**Observation and verification.** Three methods:

```
$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep "ls_in_port_sec_l2"
  table=0 (ls_in_port_sec_l2), priority=50,
    match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == {AA:BB:CC:DD:EE:01}),
    action=(next;)

$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=8 | grep "metadata=0x1"
  cookie=0x1, table=8, n_packets=523, dl_src=AA:BB:CC:DD:EE:01,
  metadata=0x1, actions=resubmit(,9)

$ ovn-trace ls1 'inport=="lsp-vm1" && eth.src==BB:BB:BB:BB:BB:BB && eth.dst==CC:..'
  → ingress(dp="ls1", inport="lsp-vm1")
    0. ls_in_port_sec_l2 (no match)  /* drops at default priority 0 */
    drop;
```

**Source code reference.** Verified at OVN baseline branch-22.03, tag v22.03.8:
- `northd/northd.c:5615` `build_lswitch_input_port_sec_op()` and `northd/northd.c:5666` `build_lswitch_input_port_sec_od()` build the flows for this stage from `Logical_Switch_Port.port_security`. The L2, IP, and ND variants share these two functions at v22.03.8; the suffix split into `_l2` / `_ip` / `_nd` landed in branch-24.03+.
- `controller/lflow.c` `consider_logical_flow()`: ovn-controller translates Logical_Flow rows into OF flows on `br-int`.
- The stage id `S_SWITCH_IN_PORT_SEC_L2 = 0` is generated by the `PIPELINE_STAGE` macro block in `northd/northd.c:103`, consumed via `northd/northd.h`.

**Real-world incident.** Q1 2024, a multi-tenant cluster: a tenant reported "VM A loses 12 seconds of ping after a live migration". Investigation: `ovn-trace` from A to B was clean, but `tcpdump` on the hypervisor showed the first ARP probe being dropped. Counting `ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=8 | grep n_packets` for the LSP of A showed the drop counter jumping by 4 in 12 seconds. Root cause: the live migration triggered a MAC re-detect, and ovn-controller needed about 10 seconds to install a new flow set with the current MAC of the VM. The old set carried the pre-migration MAC because the virsh template was wrong. Fix: update the virsh definition to keep a stable MAC, and set `lsp-set-port-security` correctly from the start.

**Synthetic exercise.** A Mininet topology with 1 LS and 2 LSPs, one legitimate VM and one attacker:

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-add ls-lab
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-lab lsp-good
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-good "AA:11:11:11:11:11"
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-good "AA:11:11:11:11:11"
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-lab lsp-bad
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-bad "BB:22:22:22:22:22"
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-bad "BB:22:22:22:22:22"
# Lab task 1: from lsp-bad, send a packet with eth.src=AA:11:11:11:11:11 and verify the drop.
# Lab task 2: remove port_security on lsp-bad (ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-bad "").
#             The spoofed packet now passes, and the victim's ARP cache is poisoned.
# Lab task 3: turn port_security back on and compare the drop counter before and after.
```
Verify each step with `ovn-trace` and `ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=8`.

**Common failures and diagnostic signals.**
- Mode A "empty port_security": a freshly booted VM cannot send packets. `ovn-nbctl lsp-get-port-security lsp-X` returns empty. Fix with `lsp-set-port-security`.
- Mode B "MAC mismatch after migration": the table 8 drop counter rises after a live migration. Reconcile the virsh MAC with the NBDB MAC.
- Mode C "REGBIT_PORT_SEC_DROP leaking": an IP spoof is flagged but the final deferred-drop flow never fires. Check whether the OVN version is older than 20.06, before this pattern existed.
- Mode D "slow stage compile": an LSP has more than 500 MACs in `port_security`. northd emits a `Reduced flow set` warning, and the LSP must be sharded.

**Comparison with other systems.** Linux iptables with `-m mac --mac-source` in bridge-mode chains is the closest equivalent. Difference: iptables is purely stateless, while the OVN stage uses deferred drop in combination with the IP and ND stages. Cisco port-security on an L2 switch (sticky MAC, max MAC count) shares the idea, but OVN has no "auto-learned max MAC count" concept; the list must be declared explicitly. NSX-T spoofguard, with its "you must declare MAC plus IP" model, is the closest semantic match to OVN `port_security`.

---

## §13.19.2 LS_IN_PRE_ACL: prepare conntrack before evaluating ACLs

**Concept.** `LS_IN_PRE_ACL` is stage **number 5** of the LS_IN pipeline (logical table 5, OF table 13). It has one job: **set `REGBIT_CONNTRACK_DEFRAG`** and call `ct_next` to pull an IP packet through the Linux kernel conntrack module, so that `ct_state` is populated for `LS_IN_ACL` to consume. If the LS has no stateful ACL, this stage does **not** emit a high-priority flow. Only a `priority=0 action=next` flow passes through. Type: a core pipeline stage, sub-type "stateful preprocessor".

**History and background.** OVN 2.5 (2016) introduced conntrack integration for stateful ACLs, at the same time as Pfaff pushed the `ct()` action into upstream OVS 2.5. Before that, OVN ACLs were only stateless (a plain L3 or L4 match, with no notion of new versus established). The `PRE_ACL` stage was split out to isolate the conntrack call site, so that an engineer debugging an ACL drop knows exactly where the packet enters the ct table, instead of having `ct()` scattered across many stages.

**Position in the architecture.** Logical stage 5 maps to OF table 13. It sits between `LS_IN_LOOKUP_FDB` and `LS_IN_PUT_FDB` (stages 3 and 4) and `LS_IN_PRE_LB` (stage 6). Scope: per-packet for each IP packet, per-datapath where only datapaths with a stateful ACL get a non-trivial flow here.

**Role.** Bridge between the OVS stateless OF abstraction and Linux netfilter stateful conntrack. Specifically: pull the packet into a conntrack zone (zone_id = datapath tunnel_key), retrieve the state, populate the `ct_state` register field, and call `next` so the downstream stage (LS_IN_ACL) can match on `ct_state`. Influence scope: `ct_state` is only valid during the **lifetime of the packet**; after the pipeline finishes, the register is cleared. The conntrack entry itself persists subject to `nf_conntrack_max` and the configured timeout.

**Why it exists.** The pain point before OVN 2.5: ACLs only matched the L4 5-tuple, so they could not distinguish "VM A initiates a connection to VM B" from "VM B replies to VM A". The engineer had to write two symmetric ACLs (allow A to B, allow B to A), which was error-prone. With stateful matching, you write one `allow-related` ACL and OVN automatically lets the reply through. For stateful matching to work, `ct_state` must be populated before the ACL match. That is the motivation for splitting out the PRE_ACL stage and calling `ct_next` early.

**Problems it solves.** Specifically, how to pull a packet into netfilter conntrack in the **right zone** before the ACL match runs. The fix: northd compiles `pre_acls` into a Logical_Flow at priority 110 that matches `(ip)` with action `reg0[0] = 1; ct_next;`. `ct_next` is an internal OVN action that maps to the OVS action `ct(table=N, zone=NXM_NX_REG13[0..15])`, which pushes the packet through conntrack with zone equal to the datapath tunnel_key (this guarantees isolation between different LSes). Scope: only IP packets; non-IP packets skip via `next`.

**Importance.** A central pipeline stage for any Logical_Switch that has stateful ACLs. If the LS has no stateful ACL (only stateless ACLs or none at all), this stage is essentially a no-op (`priority=0 action=next`). For production tenant networks with a firewall, which is the majority of cases, this is a must-know stage for debugging allow-related semantics.

**How it works.** Logical_Flow rows are emitted by `build_pre_acls()` in `northd/northd.c` when `has_stateful_acl(od)` returns true:

```
table=5 (ls_in_pre_acl), priority=110,
  match=(ip),
  action=(reg0[0] = 1; ct_next;)

table=5 (ls_in_pre_acl), priority=0,
  match=(1),
  action=(next;)
```

When compiled into OVS, `ct_next` becomes `ct(table=14, zone=NXM_NX_REG13[0..15])`. The packet recirculates through the conntrack lookup. Zone equal to `reg13[0..15]` (the datapath tunnel_key) guarantees that tenant A and tenant B use different zones and do not leak state across each other. After `ct_next`, the packet returns to the pipeline at **table 14** (= stage 6 + 8) with the `ct_state` register populated. Invariant: after this stage, every IP packet has a valid `ct_state` (`NEW`, `EST`, `REL`, `INV`, and so on).

**How an operator masters this.** (1) **Read**: know that this stage only populates `ct_state` and **does not** drop any packet on its own. (2) **Modify**: the stage is auto-generated. The way to "modify" it is to add or remove a stateful ACL on the LS with `ovn-nbctl acl-add` or `acl-del`. (3) **Observe**: use `ovs-appctl dpctl/dump-conntrack zone=<tunnel_key>` to inspect the entry after the packet passes through. (4) **Debug**: if you suspect a wrong ACL drop, the first reflex is `ovn-trace`. Look at `ct_state` at the downstream ACL stage. If `ct_state` is not populated, the root cause is in PRE_ACL (the zone does not match, the packet is not IP, or `has_stateful_acl` did not trigger).

**Classification.** Stage type: **stateful preprocessor** (subtype "ct_next invoker"). It contrasts with `LS_IN_PRE_LB` (a stateful preprocessor for LB) and `LS_OUT_PRE_ACL` (the egress ACL sibling).

**Usage workflow.**
1. Create a stateful ACL: `ovn-nbctl acl-add ls1 from-lport 1000 'ip4.src == 10.0.0.5' allow-related`.
2. Verify that northd emits the PRE_ACL flow: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep "ls_in_pre_acl"` should show priority 110 matching `ip`.
3. Trigger a packet: have VM 10.0.0.5 ping out.
4. Observe conntrack: `ovs-appctl dpctl/dump-conntrack zone=<dp_tunnel_key> | head`.
5. Verify the state is set: `ovn-trace ls1 'inport == "lsp-vm1" && ip4 && ip4.src == 10.0.0.5 && ...'` should show `ct_state` at the ACL stage.
6. Convention: if you change a stateful ACL, you may need `ovn-nbctl --wait=hv sync` so that northd recompiles.

**When something goes wrong.** Symptom: "the `allow-related` ACL does not let the reply through". Diagnostic: run `ovn-trace` and inspect `ct_state` after stage 5. If `ct_state` is empty, PRE_ACL was not called (check `has_stateful_acl`). If `ct_state` is set but the `inv` flag is on, the conntrack table is missing an entry (`nf_conntrack_max` is too low, or a zone collision). Cross-link: Part 9.24 §ct_state, Part 20.2 §ovn-trace ACL debug.

**Tightly related to.** Tightly coupled to: `LS_IN_ACL` (the downstream stage that consumes `ct_state`), the `ct_state` match field, the `ct_next` action, `REGBIT_CONNTRACK_DEFRAG` (this flag), and OVN stateful ACL (the factor that triggers northd to emit the flow). Loosely related to: the `nf_conntrack_max` sysctl, and the conntrack ALG helper module.

**Version differences.**
- OVN 2.5 (2016): introduces this stage together with stateful ACL.
- OVN 20.06 (2020): splits defrag (`ct_clear` plus `ct(commit, zone)`) into a sub-step within the same stage.
- OVN 21.03 (2021): adds IPv6 fragmentation defrag support.
- OVN 22.03 (2022): integrates with LB hairpin; stateful LB also uses PRE_ACL to set up state.
- OVN 24.03 (2024): splits `LS_IN_ACL` into `LS_IN_ACL_EVAL` and `LS_IN_ACL_ACTION`. PRE_ACL itself is unchanged, but the downstream stage differs.

**Observation and verification.**

```
$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep "ls_in_pre_acl"
  table=5 (ls_in_pre_acl), priority=110,
    match=(ip), action=(reg0[0] = 1; ct_next;)

$ ovn-trace ls1 'inport == "lsp-vm1" && ip4 && ...' --minimal
  ...
  5. ls_in_pre_acl, priority=110, match=(ip)
     reg0[0] = 1;
     ct_next;
  ct_next(ct_state=new|trk, zone=6);
  ...

$ ovs-appctl dpctl/dump-conntrack zone=6 | head -3
  tcp,orig=(src=10.0.0.5,dst=10.0.0.10,sport=4001,dport=80),
       reply=(src=10.0.0.10,dst=10.0.0.5,sport=80,dport=4001),
       protoinfo=(state=ESTABLISHED), zone=6
```

**Source code reference.**
- `northd/northd.c` `build_pre_acls()`: the main function that emits flows for this stage.
- `northd/northd.c` `has_stateful_acl(od)`: the trigger condition.
- `controller/lflow.c`: translates the `ct_next` action into OVS `ct(table=N, zone=...)`.
- `lib/actions.c` `parse_CT_NEXT()`: the parser for the `ct_next` action.
- `S_SWITCH_IN_PRE_ACL = 5` (the stage id macro).

**Real-world incident.** Q2 2024, an OpenStack Octavia LB cluster: a report came in that "external client TCP to the VIP is dropped after 30 seconds of idle time". Investigation: `ovs-appctl dpctl/dump-conntrack zone=<lb_dp_tunnel> | wc -l` showed 1.2 million entries, close to `nf_conntrack_max=1310720`. The drop happened because the conntrack table was near full, some packets could not create an entry, `ct_state` fell back to `inv`, and the stateful ACL dropped them. Root cause: PRE_ACL called `ct_next` normally, but the kernel netfilter refused to create the entry. Fix: raise `nf_conntrack_max` to 4194304 and reduce `nf_conntrack_tcp_timeout_established` from 5 days to 1 day.

**Synthetic exercise.**

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-add ls-lab
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-lab lsp-vm1
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-lab lsp-vm2
sudo ovn-nbctl acl-add ls-lab from-lport 1000 \
  'ip4.src == 10.0.0.0/24 && tcp.dst == 80' allow-related
# Lab task 1: ovn-trace one TCP SYN and verify ct_state=new+trk after stage 5.
# Lab task 2: send a reply (TCP SYN-ACK) and verify ct_state=est+trk.
# Lab task 3: delete the stateful ACL, run ovn-trace again, verify the priority 110 flow is gone.
# Lab task 4: add an ACL with `--type=stateless` and verify that PRE_ACL stays a no-op.
```

**Common failures and diagnostic signals.**
- Mode A "ct_state empty after PRE_ACL": the match `(ip)` does not match a non-IP packet, which is expected. If the packet is IP and `ct_state` is still empty, check `has_stateful_acl`.
- Mode B "ct_state=inv on every packet": `nf_conntrack_max` is nearly exhausted. Raise the sysctl.
- Mode C "zone collision": two LSes share the same tunnel_key (a rare northd bug). Restart northd.
- Mode D "PRE_ACL flow disappears after deleting the last ACL": the priority 0 no-op flow remains, but the priority 110 flow is not emitted when `!has_stateful_acl`. This is expected.

**Comparison with other systems.** The Linux iptables `raw` table `PREROUTING` chain with `-j CT --zone N` is equivalent: it also pulls the packet into conntrack in a zone and populates the state for the later rule chain. Difference: the iptables zone is a scalar number shared across the whole host namespace, while the OVN zone is the datapath tunnel_key, partitioned automatically per tenant. The Cisco ASA `inspect` engine integrates stateful inspection natively and does not expose a separate stage. The NSX-T distributed firewall is semantically equivalent but hidden under its policy API.

---

## §13.19.3 LS_IN_ACL: evaluate and apply stateful ACLs

**Concept.** `LS_IN_ACL` is logical stage **number 9** (OF table 17) and enforces the ACL decision on the ingress LS pipeline. Every row of the NBDB `ACL` table (attached to `Logical_Switch.acls` or `Port_Group.acls`) is compiled by northd into one or more Logical_Flow rows in this stage, matching `NB.match` with action `NB.action` (`allow`, `allow-related`, `drop`, or `reject`). Type: a core pipeline stage, sub-type "policy enforcement".

**History and background.** OVN 2.4 (2015) introduced stateless ACL. OVN 2.5 (2016) added stateful `allow-related`. OVN 21.06 (2021) added the `ACL.tier` column for hierarchical priority, plus `meter` for rate-limited logging. OVN 22.03 (2022) integrated Conjunctive match for large `Address_Set` (this reduces the cartesian explosion). OVN 24.03 (2024) split this stage into `LS_IN_ACL_EVAL` and `LS_IN_ACL_ACTION` to isolate the match from the action (helpful for more complex tiered policy). The curriculum baseline OVN 22.03 still uses the merged stage.

**Position in the architecture.** Logical stage 9 maps to OF table 17. It runs after `LS_IN_PRE_ACL` (stage 5, which sets `ct_state`), `LS_IN_PRE_LB` (stage 6), `LS_IN_LOOKUP_FDB` (stages 3 and 4), and `LS_IN_PRE_HAIRPIN` (stages 7 and 8). After ACL comes `LS_IN_QOS_*`. Scope: per-packet, per-datapath.

**Role.** The center of the OVN firewall logic. Each tenant declares an ACL, northd compiles it down to this stage, and ovn-controller installs it on `br-int`. Scope: one packet, based on the `ct_state` that PRE_ACL populated and the plain L3, L4, and L2 match.

**Why it exists.** Before OVN, NSX-V and legacy Neutron used iptables on each compute node to filter VM-to-VM traffic. The configuration was distributed, prone to drift, and hard to debug. OVN proposed a centralized ACL: declare it once in NBDB, compile it automatically down to every hypervisor through SBDB, and the result is uniform. The ACL stage is the single enforcement point. The engineer only needs to know "where is the ACL attached" and "which stage enforces it", instead of chasing the rule across many layers.

**Problems it solves.** Specifically, how to implement a declarative firewall on a multi-tenant overlay with three requirements: (a) stateful (let replies through automatically), (b) high-cardinality match (1000+ source IPs via `Address_Set`), and (c) priority-based override. The fix: combine `ct_state` (populated at PRE_ACL) with the `NB.match` expression. `consider_acl()` compiles the row into a flow with priority equal to `NB.priority + 1000` (the offset reserves room for the default deny), and emits the action sequence `ct(commit, zone=...)` for `allow-related`, or `drop` or `tcp_reset` for deny.

**Importance.** An absolutely central pipeline stage. Every OVN tenant network with a firewall traverses it. Without understanding the compile path from NBDB ACL through Logical_Flow to the OF flow on br-int, an engineer cannot debug the class of bug "ACL allow is clearly set but the packet is still dropped".

**How it works.** `build_acls()` in `northd/northd.c` (around line 6688 on branch-22.03 per Part 13.3) iterates over the datapaths that have ACLs and calls `consider_acl()` for each row. Each ACL produces a template flow:

```
table=9 (ls_in_acl), priority=2002,
  match=(reg0[0] == 1 && (ip4.src == $set_a && tcp.dst == 80)),
  action=(reg0[1] = 1; ct_commit { ct_label.blocked = 0; }; next;)

table=9 (ls_in_acl), priority=1,
  match=(ip),
  action=(reg0[1] = 1; next;)

table=9 (ls_in_acl), priority=65535,
  match=(ct.inv || (ct.new && ct.est)),
  action=(drop;)
```

Priority encoding: `NB.priority + 1000` (the offset reserves the bottom 1000 priorities for default-allow and reply handling). The `allow-related` action expands to `ct_commit { ct_label.blocked = 0 } ; next`, so conntrack tracks the entry and stamps `blocked=0` (the egress ACL stage can read this later). The end of the stage has three auxiliary flows: (1) the reply path `ct.est && !ct.rpl` calls `next`, (2) the default deny for `ct.inv` calls `drop`, and (3) a default `priority=0` flow calls `next` for LSes that have no stateful ACL.

**How an operator masters this.** (1) **Read**: understand the priority encoding (NBDB priority plus 1000), the tier handling, and the conjunction action for a large `Address_Set`. (2) **Modify**: `ovn-nbctl acl-add ls1 from-lport 1000 'match' action`. (3) **Observe**: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_in_acl` shows the compiled flow, and `ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=17 | grep "metadata=0x..."` shows the physical flow. (4) **Debug**: run `ovn-trace` on a packet and inspect which flow matches at stage 9, what the action is, and whether `ct_state` matches your expectation.

**Classification.** Stage type: **policy enforcement** (subtype "stateful firewall"). It contrasts with `LS_OUT_ACL` (the egress sibling), `LS_IN_PRE_ACL` (state setup), and `LS_IN_LB` (stateful LB).

**Usage workflow.**
1. Create an `Address_Set`: `ovn-nbctl create Address_Set name=set_a addresses='"10.0.0.5","10.0.0.6"'`.
2. Add an allow ACL: `ovn-nbctl acl-add ls1 from-lport 2000 'ip4.src == $set_a && tcp.dst == 80' allow-related`.
3. Add a default deny ACL: `ovn-nbctl acl-add ls1 from-lport 1 'ip4' drop`.
4. Verify compilation: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_in_acl` should show two flows at priority 3000 and 1001.
5. Test: a VM in `set_a` should reach VIP:80; a VM outside the set should be dropped.
6. Audit logging: enable `meter` on the ACL log and inspect with `journalctl -u ovn-controller | grep acl-log`.

**When something goes wrong.** Symptom: "the ACL allow is clearly set but the packet is still dropped". Diagnostic flow:
- Step 1: run `ovn-trace` and look at which flow matches at stage 9. If it drops, read the reason (a `ct.inv` match, or the default deny at priority 65535).
- Step 2: if it is `ct.inv`, check PRE_ACL and conntrack.
- Step 3: if it matches an NBDB ACL drop, inspect the priority encoding (is there a higher-priority ACL?).

Cross-link: Part 9.24 §ct_state, Part 13.3 §build_acls, Part 20.2 §ACL drop debug.

**Tightly related to.** Tightly coupled to: the NBDB `ACL` table, `Port_Group`, `Address_Set`, `LS_IN_PRE_ACL` (state source), the `ct_commit` action, `REGBIT_ACL_HINT`, `meter` (log rate-limit), and `LS_OUT_ACL` (the egress sibling). Loosely related to: iptables (the layer below), and the OpenStack Security Group API (the layer above).

**Version differences.**
- OVN 2.4 (2015): stateless ACL only.
- OVN 2.5 (2016): stateful `allow-related`.
- OVN 21.06 (2021): the `tier` column for hierarchical priority, plus `meter` for log rate-limiting.
- OVN 22.03 (2022): Conjunction action for large `Address_Set` (more than 16 elements).
- OVN 24.03 (2024): splits the stage into `EVAL` and `ACTION`.
- OVN curriculum baseline 22.03: uses the merged stage with Conjunction support.

**Observation and verification.**

```
$ ovn-nbctl acl-list ls1
  from-lport 2000 (ip4.src == $set_a && tcp.dst == 80) allow-related

$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep "ls_in_acl"
  table=9 (ls_in_acl), priority=3000,
    match=(reg0[0] == 1 && ip4.src == $set_a && tcp.dst == 80),
    action=(reg0[1] = 1; ct_commit { ct_label.blocked = 0; }; next;)

$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=17 | grep "metadata=0x6" | head -2
  cookie=0xN, table=17, n_packets=1234, priority=3000, ...,
    actions=ct(commit,zone=6,exec(load:0->NXM_NX_CT_LABEL[0])),resubmit(,18)
```

**Source code reference.**
- `northd/northd.c` `build_acls()` line 6688+: the main function.
- `northd/northd.c` `consider_acl()` line 6333+: per-row compile.
- `lib/lflow.h` `S_SWITCH_IN_ACL = 9`.
- `controller/lflow.c`: translates `ct_commit` into the OVS action.
- `lib/actions.c` `format_CT_COMMIT()`: parser for the action.

**Real-world incident.** Q2 2024, a multi-tenant DC: a tenant reported "Web to DB stops working after adding ACL log". Investigation: `ovn-trace` showed that stage 9 matched a drop flow at priority 65535 (`ct.inv`). The conntrack zone of the LS-DB had entries with the INVALID flag. Root cause: the ACL log used `meter=10/s`, which was too low. When traffic spiked, the meter was exceeded, some packets took the slow path, conntrack timing raced, and some entries were marked INVALID. Fix: raise the meter to 100/s and reduce the log severity. After the fix, the drop count returned to zero.

**Synthetic exercise.**

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-add ls-lab
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-lab lsp-vm1
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-lab lsp-vm2
sudo ovn-nbctl acl-add ls-lab from-lport 2000 \
  'ip4.src == 10.0.0.5 && tcp.dst == 80' allow-related
sudo ovn-nbctl acl-add ls-lab from-lport 1 'ip4' drop
# Lab task 1: ovn-trace from 10.0.0.5 to 10.0.0.10:80 and verify the match at priority 3000.
# Lab task 2: ovn-trace from 10.0.0.6 to 10.0.0.10:80 and verify it hits the default drop.
# Lab task 3: add a higher-priority ACL override and verify the priority order.
# Lab task 4: switch to an Address_Set of 50 IPs and verify the Conjunction action appears.
```

**Common failures and diagnostic signals.**
- Mode A "Conjunction explosion": the `Address_Set` is not using Conjunction, so the flow count is the cartesian product (100 IPs by 100 IPs = 10000 flows). `ovn-sbctl lflow-list | wc -l` rises sharply.
- Mode B "ct_state mismatch": `allow-related` is set but the reply is dropped. The cause is a conntrack zone collision or `ct.inv`.
- Mode C "priority conflict": two ACLs share the same priority. northd orders them by UUID, which is not deterministic. Use distinct priorities.
- Mode D "tier does not sort correctly": the new `ACL.tier` (since 21.06) is missing or all zero, so northd falls back to NB priority order.

**Comparison with other systems.** The Linux iptables `FORWARD` chain stateful filter is the closest equivalent. It also uses nf_conntrack, with the same `allow-related` semantics through `--state ESTABLISHED,RELATED`. Difference: OVN ACL is declarative and centralized in NBDB, while iptables is imperative and per-host. NSX-T DFW (Distributed Firewall) is semantically equivalent (declarative, distributed, stateful), but the API differs. The classic Cisco ACL is stateless only; ASA fixup adds stateful inspection. The AWS Security Group is stateful with `allow-related` semantics but has no explicit deny rule (only allow plus an implicit default-deny).

---

## §13.19.4 LS_IN_LB: Load Balancer DNAT on ingress LS

**Concept.** `LS_IN_LB` is logical stage **number 12** (OF table 20) and performs the Load_Balancer DNAT. It matches `VIP:port`, picks a backend pool member by hash, and calls the `ct_lb` action to commit a conntrack entry with the NAT mapping. Type: a core pipeline stage, sub-type "L4 load balancer plus DNAT".

**History and background.** OVN 2.4 (2015) introduced a basic LB with uniform 5-tuple hashing. OVN 21.06 (2021) added a distributed LB that runs on every hypervisor instead of being centralized on a gateway. OVN 22.03 (2022) added hairpin SNAT (when the client VM and the backend VM live on the same LS). OVN 24.03 (2024) added `Load_Balancer.options:affinity_timeout` for session stickiness.

**Position in the architecture.** Logical stage 12 maps to OF table 20. It runs after `LS_IN_PRE_LB` (stage 6, which sets `REGBIT_CONNTRACK_NAT`) and `LS_IN_LB_AFF_*` (stages 10 and 11, sticky session check), and before `LS_IN_ACL_HINT` (stage 13). Scope: per-packet, per-datapath.

**Role.** The endpoint of the LB DNAT path: rewrite the destination IP from the VIP to the specific backend. The conntrack entry is committed here so that the reply path can reverse the mapping (UNDNAT at egress). Scope: the lifetime of the connection (the entry exists until it times out).

**Why it exists.** Before OVN, OpenStack Octavia used a separate HAProxy VM for LB. That VM was a single point of failure with high latency. OVN proposed a distributed LB built into the pipeline: every hypervisor load-balances for its own VIP, removing the choke point. The LB stage is the per-hypervisor execution point.

**Problems it solves.** Specifically, perform L4 load balancing with three requirements: (a) consistent hashing so that the same client always lands on the same backend (sticky), (b) commit a conntrack entry so that the reply path reverses the DNAT correctly, and (c) support hairpin when the backend equals the source. The fix: the `ct_lb` action with `hash_fields="ip_src,ip_dst,tp_src,tp_dst,ip_proto"` produces a hash and picks a backend with `hash mod N_backend`, then commits conntrack with `nat(dst=<backend>:<port>)`. Scope: only packets with `ct.new`; the reply path goes through `LR_OUT_UNSNAT` and `LR_OUT_UNDNAT`.

**Importance.** A central pipeline stage for cloud workloads. The Octavia OVN provider uses this stage; every VIP that publishes a service traverses it. A cloud network engineer must know this stage.

**How it works.** `build_lb_rules()` in `northd/northd.c` iterates over the `Load_Balancer` references attached to the LS and emits per-VIP flows:

```
table=12 (ls_in_lb), priority=110,
  match=(ct.new && ip4 && ip4.dst == 10.0.0.100 && tcp.dst == 80),
  action=(reg0[2] = 1;
          ct_lb(backends=192.168.1.5:80,192.168.1.6:80,
                hash_fields="ip_src,tp_src");)

table=12 (ls_in_lb), priority=0,
  match=(1),
  action=(next;)
```

When compiled into OVS, `ct_lb` becomes `ct(commit, table=N, zone=..., nat(dst=backend))`. `hash_fields` controls the consistent hashing: usually the 5-tuple, so each connection sticks to one backend. If `Load_Balancer.selection_fields` is set differently (for example, only `ip_src`), the hash uses only that field, giving stickiness by source IP. Invariant: the same `(ip_src, tp_src)` pair targeting the same VIP always lands on the same backend until the backend list changes.

**How an operator masters this.** (1) **Read**: understand `hash_fields` and sticky semantics. (2) **Modify**: `ovn-nbctl lb-add lb-web 10.0.0.100:80 192.168.1.5:80,192.168.1.6:80` followed by `ovn-nbctl ls-lb-add ls1 lb-web`. (3) **Observe**: `ovs-appctl dpctl/dump-conntrack zone=<dp> | grep <vip>` shows the NAT entry. (4) **Debug**: run `ovn-trace` on a packet to the VIP and watch which backend stage 12 selects.

**Classification.** Stage type: **L4 LB plus DNAT** (subtype "stateful balanced DNAT"). It contrasts with: `LR_IN_DNAT` (north-south DNAT without a hash) and `LS_IN_NAT_HAIRPIN` (hairpin SNAT for self-LB).

**Usage workflow.**
1. Create the LB: `ovn-nbctl lb-add lb-web "10.0.0.100:80" "192.168.1.5:80,192.168.1.6:80"`.
2. Attach the LB to the LS: `ovn-nbctl ls-lb-add ls1 lb-web`.
3. (Optional) Make it sticky: `ovn-nbctl set Load_Balancer lb-web selection_fields=ip_src`.
4. Verify compilation: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_in_lb` should show a priority 110 flow.
5. Test: send 5 TCP requests from a client to the VIP and count how many landed on each backend (the ratio should be close to 50/50 with uniform hashing).
6. Sticky test: from the same client (same `ip_src`), 100 percent of requests should land on the same backend.

**When something goes wrong.** Symptom: "the VIP is unreachable for new connections after the cluster scales". Diagnostic:
- Step 1: `ovn-trace` from the client to the VIP and watch which flow matches at stage 12.
- Step 2: if no priority 110 flow matches, check whether the LB is attached: `ovn-nbctl ls-lb-list ls1`.
- Step 3: if it matches but the chosen backend is unhealthy, inspect `Service_Monitor` health status.
- Step 4: if the conntrack table is near full, NAT fails and `ct.new` packets are dropped.

Cross-link: Part 13.3 §LB compile, Part 9.24 §ct_state, Part 20.2 §LB drop debug.

**Tightly related to.** Tightly coupled to: the NBDB `Load_Balancer` table, `LS_IN_PRE_LB` (state setup), the `ct_lb` action, `Service_Monitor` (health check), `LS_IN_LB_AFF_*` (sticky-session siblings), `LS_IN_NAT_HAIRPIN` (hairpin handling), and `LR_OUT_UNSNAT` and `LR_OUT_UNDNAT` (reverse path). Loosely related to: HAProxy and Nginx (alternative LBs outside OVN).

**Version differences.**
- OVN 2.4 (2015): LB centralized on a gateway chassis.
- OVN 21.06 (2021): distributed LB on every hypervisor.
- OVN 22.03 (2022): hairpin SNAT integration; LB can be attached to an LS instead of only an LR.
- OVN 23.06 (2023): `Service_Monitor` health check automatically removes a backend that is down.
- OVN 24.03 (2024): `affinity_timeout` for sticky session with expiry; SCTP support.

**Observation and verification.**

```
$ ovn-nbctl lb-list
  UUID    LB        PROTO  VIP             IPs
  abc...  lb-web    tcp    10.0.0.100:80   192.168.1.5:80,192.168.1.6:80

$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep "ls_in_lb"
  table=12 (ls_in_lb), priority=110,
    match=(ct.new && ip4 && ip4.dst == 10.0.0.100 && tcp.dst == 80),
    action=(reg0[2] = 1;
            ct_lb(backends=192.168.1.5:80,192.168.1.6:80);)

$ ovs-appctl dpctl/dump-conntrack zone=6 | grep 10.0.0.100
  tcp,orig=(src=10.0.0.5,dst=10.0.0.100,sport=4001,dport=80),
       reply=(src=192.168.1.5,dst=10.0.0.5,sport=80,dport=4001),
       protoinfo=(state=ESTABLISHED), zone=6
```

**Source code reference.**
- `northd/northd.c` `build_lb_rules()`: the main function that emits LB flows.
- `northd/northd.c` `build_lswitch_lflows_pre_lb()`: the PRE_LB sibling stage.
- `lib/actions.c` `parse_CT_LB()`: parser for the `ct_lb` action.
- `lib/lflow.h` `S_SWITCH_IN_LB = 12`.
- `controller/lflow.c`: translates `ct_lb` into OVS `ct(commit, nat(...))`.

**Real-world incident.** Q1 2024, a production cloud: VIP `10.0.0.100:80` reported "drops new connections after about 10000 active sessions". Investigation: `ovs-appctl dpctl/dump-conntrack zone=6 | wc -l` returned 1.31 million, hitting `nf_conntrack_max=1310720`. The backends were healthy and the LB compiled flow correctly, but the `ct_lb` action could not commit because the conntrack table was full, so the packet was dropped. Fix: raise `nf_conntrack_max` to 4194304 and reduce `nf_conntrack_tcp_timeout_close_wait` from 60 seconds to 30 seconds. The drop count returned to zero after 5 minutes. Cross-link: Part 13.3 §LB scaling.

**Synthetic exercise.**

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-add ls-lab
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-lab lsp-client
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-lab lsp-be1
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-lab lsp-be2
sudo ovn-nbctl lb-add lb-web "10.0.0.100:80" "10.0.0.5:80,10.0.0.6:80"
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-lb-add ls-lab lb-web
# Lab task 1: from the client send 100 TCP requests to the VIP and count the hit ratio per backend.
# Lab task 2: set selection_fields=ip_src and verify the same client always lands on the same backend.
# Lab task 3: stop be1 so Service_Monitor marks it down and verify 100 percent of traffic shifts to be2.
# Lab task 4: hairpin test (have be1 reach the VIP of itself) and observe NAT_HAIRPIN.
```

**Common failures and diagnostic signals.**
- Mode A "conntrack table full": `nf_conntrack_count / nf_conntrack_max > 95 percent`, so new connections are dropped.
- Mode B "unhealthy backend still receives packets": `Service_Monitor` is disabled or the check interval is too slow. Enable it and reduce the interval.
- Mode C "sticky session is not sticky": the default `selection_fields` is the 5-tuple, so each new `src_port` lands on a different backend. Set `selection_fields=ip_src`.
- Mode D "hairpin loop": the backend equals the client on the same LS, and `Load_Balancer.options:hairpin_snat_ip` is not set, so the packet loops. Set the option.

**Comparison with other systems.** Linux IPVS via `ipvsadm` is the direct analog: L4 LB with hashing, and NAT mode commits a conntrack entry. Difference: OVN is distributed on every hypervisor, while IPVS is centralized. AWS NLB is semantically equivalent (L4, consistent hash, sticky) but is a managed service. HAProxy L4 mode is similar but runs in userspace and is slower. Cisco ACE and F5 BIG-IP are enterprise-grade L4 to L7 systems.

---

## §13.19.5 LS_IN_DHCP_OPTIONS: respond to DHCPDISCOVER and DHCPREQUEST natively in the pipeline

**Concept.** `LS_IN_DHCP_OPTIONS` is logical stage **number 19** (OF table 27) and runs a DHCP server directly inside the OVN pipeline, with no external dnsmasq daemon. It matches DHCPDISCOVER and DHCPREQUEST UDP packets and calls `put_dhcp_opts` to build the DHCPOFFER or DHCPACK reply directly in the kernel datapath. Type: a core pipeline stage, sub-type "inline DHCP server".

**History and background.** OVN 2.6 (2016) introduced native inline DHCPv4 (Pfaff and Reddy proposed it to drop the dnsmasq dependency). OVN 2.8 (2017) added DHCPv6. OVN 22.03 (2022) added support for option 121 (classless static route) and option 119 (domain search list). OVN 24.03 (2024) integrated with IPAM for dynamic IP allocation.

**Position in the architecture.** Logical stage 19 maps to OF table 27. It runs after the ACL stage (9) and the LB stage (12), and before ARP_RESPONDER (stage 20+) and the final L2 lookup (stage 27). Scope: per-packet (DHCP packets only), per-LSP (each LSP can reference its own `DHCP_Options`).

**Role.** Reply to DHCP requests from a VM and assign IP, gateway, DNS, and lease time, without any external component. Scope: one packet (DHCPDISCOVER or DHCPREQUEST), reply generated directly in the kernel datapath.

**Why it exists.** Before OVN 2.6, OpenStack Neutron deployed a dnsmasq instance on the network node for each tenant network. Management was complex (one process per tenant), the network node was a single point of failure, and latency was high because packets had to traverse the gateway. OVN proposed inline DHCP: each hypervisor replies to its own VMs, removing the network node bottleneck for DHCP traffic.

**Problems it solves.** Specifically, provide DHCP service to VMs without an external process. The fix: northd compiles the NB `DHCP_Options` row (subnet, `server_id`, gateway, DNS, `lease_time`, classless static route) into a Logical_Flow that matches DHCPDISCOVER and DHCPREQUEST and runs `put_dhcp_opts(...)`. ovn-controller translates this into an OVS extended action executed directly in the kernel datapath: replace the DHCP payload with a DHCPOFFER or DHCPACK, swap the source and destination MAC and IP, and send the packet back to the client. Scope: a full DHCP server, excluding DHCPv6 SLAAC (Router Advertisement does not go through this stage).

**Importance.** A central pipeline stage. Every VM bootstrap traverses it. If the stage is broken, a VM cannot get an IP and therefore cannot boot. This is must-know material for the on-call cloud network engineer.

**How it works.** `build_lswitch_dhcp_options_and_response()` in `northd/northd.c` iterates over the LSPs that have `dhcpv4_options` set and emits a per-LSP flow:

```
table=19 (ls_in_dhcp_options), priority=100,
  match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == AA:BB:CC:DD:EE:01 &&
         ip4.src == 0.0.0.0 && ip4.dst == 255.255.255.255 &&
         udp.src == 68 && udp.dst == 67),
  action=(reg0[3] = put_dhcp_opts(offerip = 10.0.0.5,
                                   netmask = 255.255.255.0,
                                   router = 10.0.0.1,
                                   server_id = 10.0.0.1,
                                   lease_time = 3600,
                                   dns_server = {8.8.8.8});
          next;)

table=19 (ls_in_dhcp_options), priority=0,
  match=(1),
  action=(next;)
```

The `put_dhcp_opts` action is an OVN extended action (not standard OpenFlow). ovn-controller compiles it into an OVS action sequence. The fallback path uses a `controller(userspace)` callback handled in userspace, but since OVS 2.7 there is an optimized in-kernel path. `reg0[3]` is 1 on success and 0 on failure (for example, `offerip` outside the subnet). The next stage (`LS_IN_DHCP_RESPONSE`, table 20) checks `reg0[3]` and emits the reply. Invariant: a DHCP packet that passes this stage successfully will appear in the downstream pipeline as a DHCPOFFER or DHCPACK reply packet.

**How an operator masters this.** (1) **Read**: understand the `DHCP_Options` column structure (subnet, `server_id`, gateway, DNS, `lease_time`, classless static route). (2) **Modify**: `ovn-nbctl dhcp-options-create 10.0.0.0/24` followed by `ovn-nbctl dhcp-options-set-options <uuid> server_id=10.0.0.1 lease_time=3600 router=10.0.0.1 dns_server='{8.8.8.8}'`, then attach to the LSP with `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-dhcpv4-options lsp1 <dhcp_uuid>`. (3) **Observe**: `tcpdump` on the tap interface, or `ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=27 | grep put_dhcp_opts`. (4) **Debug**: if a VM is stuck at DHCP, simulate a DHCPDISCOVER with `ovn-trace` and check whether stage 19 matches.

**Classification.** Stage type: **inline DHCP server** (subtype "native DHCPv4"). It contrasts with: `LS_IN_DHCP_RESPONSE` (stage 20, emits the reply), `LS_IN_DNS_LOOKUP` (a similar stage for DNS), and `LR_IN_IP_INPUT` (handles packets destined to the LR itself).

**Usage workflow.**
1. Create the `DHCP_Options`: `dhcp_uuid=$(ovn-nbctl create DHCP_Options cidr=10.0.0.0/24 options='"server_id"="10.0.0.1" "lease_time"="3600" "router"="10.0.0.1"')`.
2. Create the LS and LSP: `ovn-nbctl ls-add ls1 && ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls1 lsp-vm1`.
3. Set the address to dynamic: `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-vm1 "AA:BB:CC:DD:EE:01 dynamic"`.
4. Attach the DHCP options: `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-dhcpv4-options lsp-vm1 $dhcp_uuid`.
5. Verify compilation: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_in_dhcp_options`.
6. Boot the VM: DHCPDISCOVER, DHCPOFFER 10.0.0.5, DHCPREQUEST, DHCPACK.
7. Verify the lease: confirm from inside the VM that it received the IP.

**When something goes wrong.** Symptom: "the VM is stuck at DHCP and never gets an IP". Diagnostic flow:
- Step 1: `tcpdump` on the VM tap interface and see whether the DHCPDISCOVER appears (if not, the issue is inside the VM).
- Step 2: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_in_dhcp_options` and see whether a priority 100 flow exists.
- Step 3: if the flow is missing, check `ovn-nbctl lsp-get-dhcpv4-options lsp-vm1`.
- Step 4: if the flow exists, simulate a packet with `ovn-trace` and watch stage 19 match the `put_dhcp_opts` action.
- Step 5: if `offerip` is out of subnet, compare `DHCP_Options.cidr` with the LSP IP.

Cross-link: Part 13.10 §DHCP native, Part 20.0 §VM bootstrap troubleshooting.

**Tightly related to.** Tightly coupled to: the NBDB `DHCP_Options` table, the NBDB `Logical_Switch_Port.dhcpv4_options` column, `LS_IN_DHCP_RESPONSE` (stage 20, emits the reply), the `put_dhcp_opts` action, and `REGBIT_DHCP_OPTS_RESULT`. Loosely related to: dnsmasq (the external alternative), and cloud-init (which consumes the IP).

**Version differences.**
- OVN 2.6 (2016): introduces native DHCPv4.
- OVN 2.8 (2017): adds DHCPv6.
- OVN 21.06 (2021): IPAM allocates IPs from the subnet automatically.
- OVN 22.03 (2022): option 121 (classless static route) and option 119 (domain search list).
- OVN 23.06 (2023): adds Boot Options (PXE) support.
- OVN 24.03 (2024): IPAM integrates with `DHCP_Options` auto-tracking.

**Observation and verification.**

```
$ ovn-nbctl dhcp-options-list
  abc... 10.0.0.0/24

$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep "ls_in_dhcp_options"
  table=19 (ls_in_dhcp_options), priority=100,
    match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == AA:BB:CC:DD:EE:01 &&
           ip4.src == 0.0.0.0 && ip4.dst == 255.255.255.255 &&
           udp.src == 68 && udp.dst == 67),
    action=(reg0[3] = put_dhcp_opts(offerip=10.0.0.5, ...); next;)

$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=27 | grep put_dhcp_opts | head -1
  cookie=0xN, table=27, n_packets=4, ...,
    actions=load:0->NXM_NX_REG0[3],controller(userdata=...),resubmit(,28)

$ tcpdump -nei tap-vm1 udp port 67 or port 68
  IP 0.0.0.0.68 > 255.255.255.255.67: BOOTP/DHCP, Request from AA:..., DHCPDISCOVER
  IP 10.0.0.1.67 > 10.0.0.5.68:       BOOTP/DHCP, Reply, DHCPOFFER, lease 3600
```

**Source code reference.**
- `northd/northd.c` `build_lswitch_dhcp_options_and_response()`: the main function.
- `lib/actions.c` `parse_put_dhcp_opts()`: parser for the action.
- `controller/pinctrl.c` `pinctrl_handle_put_dhcp_opts()`: the userspace handler for the fallback path.
- `lib/lflow.h` `S_SWITCH_IN_DHCP_OPTIONS = 19`.
- `lib/dhcp.h`: DHCP option code definitions.

**Real-world incident.** 2024 production: a freshly deployed tenant network had VMs stuck at "Waiting for DHCP". Investigation: `tcpdump` on the tap interface showed the DHCPDISCOVER but no reply. `ovn-sbctl lflow-list | grep ls_in_dhcp_options` showed a flow with `offerip = 192.168.1.5`, but the subnet in `DHCP_Options` was `10.0.0.0/24`. Root cause: the operator typo'd `cidr=192.168.1.0/24` in `DHCP_Options` while the VM IP was in subnet `10.0.0.0/24`, so `put_dhcp_opts` returned 0 (failure) and no reply was emitted. Fix: `ovn-nbctl set DHCP_Options <uuid> cidr=10.0.0.0/24 options:server_id=10.0.0.1`. After the fix, the VM received its IP within 5 seconds.

**Synthetic exercise.**

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-add ls-lab
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-lab lsp-vm1
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-vm1 "AA:11:11:11:11:11 dynamic"
DHCP=$(sudo ovn-nbctl create DHCP_Options cidr=10.0.0.0/24 \
       options='"server_id"="10.0.0.1" "lease_time"="3600" "router"="10.0.0.1"')
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-dhcpv4-options lsp-vm1 $DHCP
# Lab task 1: ovn-trace a simulated DHCPDISCOVER and verify stage 19 matches.
# Lab task 2: add option 6 dns_server={8.8.8.8} and verify the reply carries the DNS option.
# Lab task 3: change the cidr to a wrong value (192.168.1.0/24) and verify put_dhcp_opts fails.
# Lab task 4: remove dhcpv4_options from the LSP and verify stage 19 no longer matches.
```

**Common failures and diagnostic signals.**
- Mode A "DHCP_Options not attached to LSP": `ovn-nbctl lsp-get-dhcpv4-options lsp1` returns empty. Re-attach.
- Mode B "subnet mismatch": `offerip` is outside the cidr, so `put_dhcp_opts` fails. Reconcile the cidr.
- Mode C "server_id missing": the option is required by RFC 2131; some clients reject the reply without it. Set the option.
- Mode D "lease_time too short": below 60 seconds triggers a DHCP renewal storm. Raise to at least 3600 seconds.
- Mode E "DHCPv6 needs SLAAC": IPv6 typically uses SLAAC via Router Advertisement, not `DHCP_Options`. Use `Logical_Router_Port.ipv6_ra_configs` instead.

**Comparison with other systems.** Linux dnsmasq is the analog DHCP server: similar function (assign IP, options), but dnsmasq is an external userspace daemon, while OVN runs inline in the pipeline (in the kernel datapath). The ISC DHCP server is enterprise-grade but also external. Cisco IOS `ip dhcp pool` is equivalent in declaration model. The AWS DHCP option set is semantically equivalent (declarative options) but managed; OVN manages everything itself. OpenStack Neutron before OVN used a per-network dnsmasq, which OVN inline replaces.

---

## §13.19.6 LS_IN_L2_LKUP — quyết định outport L2 cuối cùng của ingress LS

**Khái niệm.** `LS_IN_L2_LKUP` là stage logic **số 24** (OF table 32) — **stage cuối** của pipeline LS_IN. Trách nhiệm duy nhất: match `eth.dst` → set `outport` (tức `MFF_LOG_OUTPORT`, register reg15 trong OVS) chỉ tới Logical_Switch_Port đích. Sau khi stage này set xong outport, packet rời nhánh ingress LS qua action `output;` để vào pipeline egress (`LS_OUT_PRE_ACL` → `LS_OUT_DELIVERY`). Loại: **pipeline stage cornerstone**, sub-loại "L2 destination lookup + forwarding decision".

**Lịch sử + bối cảnh.** Stage có mặt từ OVN 2.4 (2015) như là core của pipeline LS — bản chất chính là chức năng MAC learning của một switch. OVN 20.06 (2020) thêm cơ chế "known dst flood" (flood kiểm soát chỉ tới các LSP có `addresses="unknown"`) thay vì flood toàn bộ. OVN 22.03 (2022) thêm bảng FDB `MAC_Binding`-style cho LSP type "vtep" và `localnet` để giảm broadcast leak. OVN 24.03 (2024) tích hợp với cờ `MLF_RCV_FROM_RAMP` để tránh hairpin loop khi packet đến từ ramp switch (RFC ramp).

**Vị trí trong kiến trúc.** Stage logic 24 ⇒ OF table 32. Đứng ngay sau `LS_IN_HAIRPIN` (logical 23) và trước nhánh egress qua action `output;` (chuyển sang OF table 33+ cho LS_OUT). Trên br-int của hypervisor, stage này là **điểm chuyển trọng tâm**: trước nó pipeline làm "policy" (security, ACL, LB, ARP responder); sau nó pipeline làm "delivery". Scope: per-packet, per-LS datapath. Không có stage nào sau nó còn quyền đổi outport (trừ trường hợp đặc biệt egress hairpin).

**Vai trò.** Vai trò chính: **forwarding decision** trên L2 — tương đương MAC table của một bridge truyền thống. Vai trò phụ: **broadcast/multicast distributor** (khi `eth.dst` là `ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff` hoặc multicast MAC, set outport thành tập multicast `_MC_flood`). Phạm vi ảnh hưởng: 1 packet, ghi giá trị reg15 sống đến cuối pipeline egress.

**Vì sao sinh ra.** Một switch ảo bắt buộc phải có L2 lookup. Trước OVN, OpenStack Neutron-OVS dùng learn-action OpenFlow + flood-learn pattern (chậm, race condition). OVN dịch sang model **declarative**: thay vì học MAC từ traffic, NBDB liệt kê tường minh `Logical_Switch_Port.addresses`, northd compile thẳng thành flow priority 50. Điểm mạnh: deterministic, không có MAC table aging race; điểm yếu: tenant phải đăng ký MAC trước qua API, không "tự học".

**Vấn đề giải quyết.** Cụ thể: chuyển từ `eth.dst` sang outport. Cách giải: hàm `build_lswitch_destination_lookup_bmcast` + `build_lswitch_arp_nd_responder_known_ips` (`northd/northd.c`) iterate mọi LSP của LS, sinh flow priority 50 match `eth.dst == <LSP_MAC>` action `outport = <LSP_NAME>; output;`. Cho broadcast/multicast, sinh flow priority 70 match `eth.mcast` action `outport = "_MC_flood"; output;`. Cho unknown unicast (không match LSP nào), priority 0 fallback flood tới các LSP có `addresses="unknown"` — thường chỉ `localnet` port chuyển ra ngoài physical network. Phạm vi giải quyết: chỉ L2 forwarding; không xử lý conntrack (đã xong ở stage trước), không xử lý L3 (LR có pipeline riêng).

**Importance.** An absolutely central pipeline stage. Every LS ingress packet traverses it. If the stage compiles wrong (empty LSP MAC, wrong MC group), the tenant network goes completely silent. The engineer must understand that `MFF_LOG_OUTPORT` is reg15 (see §13.18), distinguish the three priority branches (50 unicast, 70 multicast, 0 unknown), and know about the FDB table fallback added in OVN 22.03+. Without this stage, an engineer cannot debug the class of bug "the tenant can ping the subnet broadcast address but unicast fails".

**Cơ chế hoạt động.** Logical_Flow tiêu biểu cho LS có 2 LSP `lsp-vm1` (MAC AA:01) và `lsp-vm2` (MAC AA:02):

```
table=24 (ls_in_l2_lkup), priority=50,
  match=(eth.dst == AA:AA:AA:AA:AA:01),
  action=(outport = "lsp-vm1"; output;)

table=24 (ls_in_l2_lkup), priority=50,
  match=(eth.dst == AA:AA:AA:AA:AA:02),
  action=(outport = "lsp-vm2"; output;)

table=24 (ls_in_l2_lkup), priority=70,
  match=(eth.mcast),
  action=(outport = "_MC_flood"; output;)

table=24 (ls_in_l2_lkup), priority=0,
  match=(1),
  action=(outport = "_MC_unknown"; output;)
```

Action `output;` không phải OF action `output:N` thuần — nó là OVN macro nhả về stage egress đầu (`LS_OUT_PRE_LB` cho unicast, hoặc clone packet cho multicast group). `_MC_flood` là multicast group OVS chứa tunnel_key của mọi LSP trên LS đó; ovn-controller install group entry tự động. Invariant: sau stage này, reg15 luôn có giá trị; nếu reg15 = 0xfffe (`_MC_unknown`) packet sẽ được flood tới tập LSP `unknown`.

**Cách kỹ sư vận hành thành thạo.** Bốn kỹ năng: (1) **Đọc**: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_in_l2_lkup` xem flow compile; `ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=32 | grep "metadata=0x<dp>"` xem flow đã install. (2) **Sửa**: thêm/sửa MAC qua `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp1 "<new_mac> <ip>"`; sau đó `ovn-nbctl --wait=hv sync`. (3) **Quan sát**: `ovn-trace ls1 'inport=="lsp1" && eth.dst==<dst_mac>'` thấy chính xác stage 24 chọn outport nào. (4) **Debug**: nếu nghi MAC mismatch, dump conntrack + reg15 qua `ofproto/trace`.

**Phân loại.** Loại stage: **L2 forwarding decision** (subtype "destination lookup"). Khác `LS_OUT_DELIVERY` (chỉ output thuần, không lookup nữa) và `LR_IN_IP_ROUTING` (L3 lookup, không phải L2). Là **terminal decision stage** của ingress LS — không stage nào sau nó còn re-evaluate outport.

**Quy trình sử dụng.** Khi cấu hình LS bình thường:
1. `ovn-nbctl ls-add ls1`
2. `ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls1 lsp-vm1`
3. `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-vm1 "AA:AA:AA:AA:AA:01 10.0.0.5"` (MAC + IP declare)
4. Verify compile: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_in_l2_lkup` thấy flow priority 50
5. Verify install: `ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=32 | grep AA:AA` thấy rule
6. Test ping giữa lsp-vm1 ↔ lsp-vm2; `ovn-trace` xác nhận stage 24 set reg15 đúng

**Khi xảy ra sự cố.** Symptom điển hình: (a) "VM ping broadcast được nhưng unicast fail" → ngay lập tức nghi MAC chưa khớp giữa NBDB và VM thật → check `ovn-nbctl lsp-get-addresses` so với `ip link show` trong VM. (b) "Tenant network im lặng sau scale-out" → kiểm tra số flow priority 50 trong table 32: nếu thiếu LSP nào nghĩa là northd compile chậm/lỗi. (c) "Broadcast flood quá tải link uplink" → xem priority 70 có chuyển hết về `localnet` không (cần segmenting MC group). Cross-link: Phần 13.2 §Logical_Switch lookup, Phần 13.16 §logical→OF table mapping.

**Liên quan mật thiết.** Tightly coupled: `MFF_LOG_OUTPORT` (đích set của stage), `_MC_flood` + `_MC_unknown` multicast group, `Logical_Switch_Port.addresses` (NBDB nguồn dữ liệu), `LS_IN_HAIRPIN` (stage liền trước), `LS_OUT_PRE_LB` / `LS_OUT_DELIVERY` (stage liền sau qua action output). Loose: ARP cache trong VM (layer trên), Linux bridge FDB (alternative không qua OVN).

**Khác biệt giữa các phiên bản.**
- OVN 2.4 (2015): chỉ unicast + flood, không có MC group concept rõ ràng
- OVN 20.06 (2020): tách `_MC_flood` thành flood "known" + "unknown" để giảm broadcast tới tập tối thiểu
- OVN 22.03 (2022): introduce FDB table cho LSP type "vtep" + "localnet" để track MAC từ external
- OVN 23.06 (2023): tối ưu compile khi LSP > 1000 (giảm số flow do chia shard logical OFTABLE)
- OVN 24.03 (2024): integrate `MLF_RCV_FROM_RAMP` để chặn hairpin loop từ ramp switch path

**Cách quan sát + xác minh.** Ba phương pháp:

```
$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep "ls_in_l2_lkup"
  table=24 (ls_in_l2_lkup), priority=50,
    match=(eth.dst == aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:01),
    action=(outport = "lsp-vm1"; output;)

$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=32 | grep "metadata=0x6"
  cookie=0x..., table=32, n_packets=1247, dl_dst=aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:01,
    metadata=0x6, actions=load:0x1->NXM_NX_REG15[],resubmit(,33)

$ ovn-trace ls1 'inport=="lsp-vm1" && eth.src==aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:01 && eth.dst==aa:aa:aa:aa:aa:02'
  → ingress(dp="ls1", inport="lsp-vm1")
    24. ls_in_l2_lkup (priority=50, match eth.dst)
        outport = "lsp-vm2";
        output;
```

**Source code.** Tham chiếu OVN branch-22.03 (baseline curriculum):
- `northd/northd.c` `build_lswitch_destination_lookup_bmcast()`: hàm chính build broadcast/multicast/unknown branches
- `northd/northd.c` `build_lswitch_arp_nd_responder_known_ips()`: build ARP responder (priority cao hơn rồi mới fall sang L2_LKUP cho non-ARP)
- `northd/northd.c` `build_lswitch_destination_lookup_unicast()`: build per-LSP priority 50 flow
- `lib/lflow.h` `S_SWITCH_IN_L2_LKUP = 24`: định nghĩa stage id
- `controller/lflow.c` `consider_logical_flow()`: dịch Logical_Flow xuống OF table 32

**Trường hợp sự cố thực tế.** Q3/2024 multi-tenant cluster: tenant báo "subnet 10.0.0.0/24 mất kết nối unicast giữa VM trong cùng LS, nhưng broadcast (ARP) vẫn đi". Investigation: `ovn-trace` từ A→B kết quả "ls_in_l2_lkup no match" → fallback `_MC_unknown` flood ra `localnet` ngoài cluster (lost). Đếm `ovn-nbctl lsp-get-addresses lsp-B` = `dynamic` (chưa allocate). Root cause: khi VM B vừa được tạo, IPAM chưa cấp xong → `Logical_Switch_Port.addresses` chưa có MAC concrete → northd không sinh flow priority 50 cho B. Fix: chờ IPAM hoàn tất (~2s) hoặc set MAC tĩnh; thêm Prometheus alert "LSP no concrete MAC > 30s".

**Bài tập synthetic.** Mininet topology 1 LS + 3 LSP gồm 2 VM + 1 localnet:

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-add ls-lab
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-lab lsp-vm1
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-vm1 "AA:AA:AA:AA:AA:01 10.0.0.5"
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-lab lsp-vm2
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-vm2 "AA:AA:AA:AA:AA:02 10.0.0.6"
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-lab ln-public
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-type ln-public localnet
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses ln-public unknown
# Lab task 1: ovn-trace từ vm1 → vm2 unicast → quan sát stage 24 priority 50 hit
# Lab task 2: ovn-trace từ vm1 → eth.dst=ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff → stage 24 priority 70 match _MC_flood
# Lab task 3: ovn-trace eth.dst=AA:AA:AA:AA:AA:99 (unknown) → priority 0 hit, flood tới ln-public
# Lab task 4: gỡ ln-public rồi lặp task 3 → quan sát packet drop hoàn toàn
```

**Lỗi thường gặp + tín hiệu chẩn đoán.**
- Mode A "LSP addresses chưa concrete (dynamic chưa cấp)": `ovn-nbctl lsp-get-addresses` chỉ "dynamic" → đợi IPAM hoặc set tĩnh
- Mode B "MAC mismatch giữa NBDB và OS VM": VM tự đổi MAC (cloud-init random) → unicast miss → reconcile MAC
- Mode C "_MC_flood quá tải": LS có > 500 LSP, broadcast storm → giảm broadcast workload (multicast IGMP snooping nếu áp dụng) hoặc shard LS
- Mode D "FDB table chưa learn cho localnet": OVN 22.03+, MAC từ external chưa learn vào FDB → tạm thời flood unknown → đợi FDB hoặc set MAC tĩnh

**So sánh với hệ khác.** Linux bridge `brctl showmacs` direct analog: cùng L2 lookup match `eth.dst` → port. Khác: bridge tự học MAC từ traffic (dynamic), OVN declarative (NBDB declare). Cisco MAC address-table tương đương ý tưởng nhưng kèm aging timer, OVN không aging vì không học. NSX-T Logical Switch L2 forwarding gần như giống hệt (cùng pattern declarative qua API), khác implementation detail. VMware vSphere DVS port-based forwarding cũng L2 lookup nhưng port-binding khác model.

---

## §13.19.7 LR_IN_ADMISSION — cổng vào ingress của Logical_Router

**Khái niệm.** `LR_IN_ADMISSION` là stage logic **số 0** của pipeline ingress trên một Logical_Router (OF table 8 — chia sẻ với `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2`, phân biệt nhờ `metadata` chứa datapath ID của LR). Vai trò: **kiểm soát admission** ở biên router. Drop packet không hợp lệ ở L2 cho LR (sai dst MAC, source loopback/multicast trên field IP source, packet đến từ port không phải LRP). Loại: **pipeline stage cornerstone**, sub-loại "L3 admission gate".

**Lịch sử + bối cảnh.** OVN 2.5 (2015) introduce Logical_Router. Stage `LR_IN_ADMISSION` là cổng đầu tiên ngay từ phiên bản đầu — semantic mượn từ Linux router behavior (kernel drop packet có dst MAC khác router MAC tại NIC ingress). OVN 20.06 (2020) thêm xử lý multicast MAC (nếu LRP join multicast group). OVN 22.03 (2022) thêm cờ `REGBIT_PKT_LARGER` để track packet size cần fragment. OVN 23.06 (2023) integrate với `Logical_Router_Port.options:gateway_mtu` để check MTU sớm.

**Vị trí trong kiến trúc.** Stage logic 0 của LR ⇒ OF table 8 (cùng table nhưng metadata khác với LS). Trước stage này chỉ có OF table 0 (port → datapath mapping). Sau stage là `LR_IN_LOOKUP_NEIGHBOR` (logical 1). Scope: per-packet, per-LRP. Chính xác hơn: chỉ packet vào LR qua một LRP "chính chủ" (eth.dst trùng MAC LRP, hoặc multicast/broadcast cho ARP) mới qua stage này; sai → drop.

**Vai trò.** Vai trò chính: **gatekeeper biên router** — bảo đảm chỉ packet đích router mới đi vào pipeline L3. Vai trò phụ: **drop sink** cho packet sai biên (LRP MAC mismatch, loopback src, all-zero src). Nếu disable stage này, mọi packet đi qua tap LR sẽ vào pipeline L3 ngay cả khi VM bên kia LS vô tình broadcast — gây xử lý L3 không cần thiết, có thể trigger ICMP error sai.

**Vì sao sinh ra.** Trước OVN, OpenStack Neutron-OVS dùng router namespace + iptables để filter packet biên router. Cách đó tốn namespace, slow path qua kernel routing. OVN abstract thẳng vào pipeline OpenFlow: stage này cài flow matching `inport == "lrp1" && eth.dst == <LRP_MAC>` action `next;`, default `drop;`. Loại bỏ namespace, fast path qua datapath. Pain point cũ: namespace router fail-over chậm; OVN giải quyết qua stage stateless trong mỗi hypervisor.

**Vấn đề giải quyết.** Cụ thể: lọc packet biên router để chỉ cho packet hợp lệ vào L3 pipeline. Cách giải: hàm `build_adm_ctrl_flows_for_lrouter` (`northd/northd.c`) iterate mọi `Logical_Router_Port` của LR, sinh flow priority 50 match `inport == "lrp-X" && (eth.dst == <LRP_MAC> || eth.mcast)` action `next;`. Default priority 0 drop. Cho IPv6, thêm flow match multicast IPv6 (FF::/8). Phạm vi: chỉ admission L2/L3-source check; routing chính do stage `LR_IN_IP_ROUTING` (logical 9) phụ trách.

**Importance.** A central pipeline stage. Every packet entering a Logical_Router traverses it. If compilation is wrong, the router goes completely silent and every east-west VM traversing the LR fails. The engineer must understand that this stage drops "lost" packets (those that reached an LR tap but whose destination MAC is not an LRP) rather than forwarding them, and that broadcast `ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff` is passed through so a later stage can handle ARP. Without this stage, the class of bug "VM cannot ping the gateway" will be debugged in the wrong place.

**Cơ chế hoạt động.** Flow tiêu biểu cho LR có 2 LRP `lrp1` (MAC RR:01) và `lrp2` (MAC RR:02):

```
table=0 (lr_in_admission), priority=50,
  match=(inport == "lrp1" && (eth.dst == RR:RR:RR:RR:RR:01 || eth.mcast)),
  action=(xreg0[0..47] = RR:RR:RR:RR:RR:01;  /* ghi src MAC sẽ dùng cho egress */
          next;)

table=0 (lr_in_admission), priority=50,
  match=(inport == "lrp2" && (eth.dst == RR:RR:RR:RR:RR:02 || eth.mcast)),
  action=(xreg0[0..47] = RR:RR:RR:RR:RR:02; next;)

table=0 (lr_in_admission), priority=100,
  match=(ip4.src == 127.0.0.0/8 || ip4.src == 224.0.0.0/4 || ip4.src == 0.0.0.0),
  action=(drop;)  /* martian source */

table=0 (lr_in_admission), priority=0,
  match=(1),
  action=(drop;)
```

Action `xreg0[0..47] = <LRP_MAC>` ghi MAC nguồn router để egress dùng làm `eth.src` (tương tự kernel router rewrite L2 header khi forward). Invariant: sau stage, nếu packet còn sống (`next;`), nó **chắc chắn** đến đúng LRP của router; xreg0 đã có MAC để stage egress dùng.

**Cách kỹ sư vận hành thành thạo.** (1) **Đọc**: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list lr1 | grep lr_in_admission` xem 2 nhánh priority 50 + 100 + 0. (2) **Sửa**: thêm/sửa LRP MAC qua `ovn-nbctl lrp-add lr1 lrp1 RR:01 10.0.0.1/24`. (3) **Quan sát**: `ovn-trace lr1 'inport=="lrp1" && eth.dst==RR:01 && ...'` thấy stage 0 match priority 50 next. (4) **Debug**: nếu packet drop ngay biên router, đếm `ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=8 | grep "metadata=0x<lr_dp>" | grep "n_packets"` xem flow priority 0 fallback (drop) có tăng không.

**Phân loại.** Loại stage: **L3 admission gate** (subtype "border filter"). Khác `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` (lọc spoof L2 trên LS, không phải biên L3) và `LR_IN_IP_INPUT` (xử lý packet đích router self, sau stage này). Stateless thuần.

**Quy trình sử dụng.**
1. `ovn-nbctl lr-add lr1`
2. `ovn-nbctl lrp-add lr1 lrp1 RR:RR:RR:RR:RR:01 10.0.0.1/24`
3. Gắn LRP vào LS: `ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls1 ls1-to-lr1 && ovn-nbctl lsp-set-type ls1-to-lr1 router && ovn-nbctl lsp-set-options ls1-to-lr1 router-port=lrp1 && ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses ls1-to-lr1 router`
4. Verify: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list lr1 | grep lr_in_admission` thấy flow priority 50
5. Test admission: từ VM bên LS gửi packet tới gateway IP → ovn-trace verify stage 0 match
6. Test drop: tự gửi packet với eth.dst = MAC bất kỳ khác RR:01 → drop counter tăng

**Khi xảy ra sự cố.** Symptom: (a) "VM không ping được gateway 10.0.0.1" → check stage 0 trong table 8 metadata LR, đặc biệt drop counter priority 0; nếu tăng có thể LRP MAC đổi mà VM ARP cache stale. (b) "Sau migrate gateway chassis, packet đi N-S fail vài giây" → stage này không phải nguyên nhân chính (xem `LR_IN_GW_REDIRECT`) nhưng kiểm tra để loại trừ. (c) "Martian source spam" → priority 100 drop count tăng → có host tenant gửi packet với source 0.0.0.0/loopback → cần bật alert.

**Liên quan mật thiết.** Tightly coupled: `Logical_Router_Port.mac` (NBDB nguồn dữ liệu MAC), `Logical_Router_Port.networks` (subnet declare), `xreg0` (register lưu LRP MAC cho egress sau), `LR_IN_LOOKUP_NEIGHBOR` (stage liền sau). Loose: ARP cache trong VM (layer trên), Linux kernel rp_filter (alternative stack ngoài OVN).

**Khác biệt giữa các phiên bản.**
- OVN 2.5 (2015): chỉ unicast match MAC; không multicast nhánh
- OVN 20.06 (2020): thêm multicast MAC pass-through cho ARP/ND
- OVN 22.03 (2022): integrate `REGBIT_PKT_LARGER` flag cho MTU check sau
- OVN 23.06 (2023): `gateway_mtu` option cho phép check MTU sớm tại stage này
- OVN 24.03 (2024): tối ưu compile khi LR có > 50 LRP (chia shard)

**Cách quan sát + xác minh.**

```
$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list lr1 | grep "lr_in_admission"
  table=0 (lr_in_admission), priority=50,
    match=(inport == "lrp1" && (eth.dst == rr:rr:rr:rr:rr:01 || eth.mcast)),
    action=(xreg0[0..47] = rr:rr:rr:rr:rr:01; next;)

$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=8 | grep "metadata=0x7"
  cookie=0x..., table=8, n_packets=512, priority=50,
    metadata=0x7,reg14=0x1,dl_dst=rr:rr:rr:rr:rr:01,
    actions=load:0xrrrrrrrrrr01->NXM_NX_XREG0[0..47],resubmit(,9)

$ ovn-trace lr1 'inport=="lrp1" && eth.src==aa:aa && eth.dst==rr:rr:rr:rr:rr:01 && ip4 && ip4.src==10.0.0.5 && ip4.dst==10.1.0.5'
  → ingress(dp="lr1", inport="lrp1")
    0. lr_in_admission (priority=50)
       xreg0[0..47] = rr:rr:rr:rr:rr:01;
       next;
```

**Source code.** Tham chiếu OVN branch-22.03:
- `northd/northd.c` `build_adm_ctrl_flows_for_lrouter()`: hàm chính
- `northd/northd.c` `build_adm_ctrl_flows_for_lrouter_port()`: per-LRP build
- `lib/lflow.h` `S_ROUTER_IN_ADMISSION = 0`: stage id LR
- `controller/lflow.c` `consider_logical_flow()` translate Logical_Flow → OF table 8

**Trường hợp sự cố thực tế.** Q2/2024 production: tenant nâng cấp gateway IP từ 10.0.0.1 → 10.0.0.254, nhưng quên update `Logical_Router_Port.mac` cho LRP. Symptom: tất cả VM trong subnet mất default route (`ping 8.8.8.8` fail, nhưng `ping 10.0.0.5` cùng subnet OK). Investigation: ovn-trace thấy stage 0 LR fallthrough priority 0 (drop). Đếm `ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=8 | grep n_packets` priority 0 tăng hàng giây. Root cause: VM ARP cache cũ trỏ MAC LRP cũ, nhưng OVN cập nhật LRP MAC mới (có thể do API chỉnh tay) → eth.dst trong packet VM gửi không khớp `Logical_Router_Port.mac` mới → drop. Fix: rollback LRP MAC về cũ (sửa MAC LRP yêu cầu coordinated ARP refresh trên mọi VM, nguy hiểm trong production).

**Bài tập synthetic.**

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl lr-add lr-lab
sudo ovn-nbctl lrp-add lr-lab lrp-lab RR:11:11:11:11:11 10.0.0.1/24
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-add ls-lab
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-lab ls-lab-to-lr
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-type ls-lab-to-lr router
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-options ls-lab-to-lr router-port=lrp-lab
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses ls-lab-to-lr router
# Lab task 1: ovn-trace packet với eth.dst=RR:11:11:11:11:11 → verify priority 50 next
# Lab task 2: ovn-trace với eth.dst=BB:BB:BB:BB:BB:BB → verify priority 0 drop
# Lab task 3: ovn-trace với ip4.src=127.0.0.1 → verify priority 100 martian drop
# Lab task 4: đổi LRP MAC sang RR:99:99:99:99:99 rồi gửi packet với eth.dst RR:11 (cũ) → drop counter tăng
```

**Lỗi thường gặp + tín hiệu chẩn đoán.**
- Mode A "ARP cache VM lệch LRP MAC": stage 0 priority 0 drop count tăng sau khi sửa LRP MAC → flush ARP cache hoặc rollback
- Mode B "LRP chưa gắn vào LS qua patch port": LSP type=router chưa set router-port → packet không bao giờ đến stage này → check lsp options
- Mode C "Martian source filter chặn legit traffic": NAT trả packet với source 0.0.0.0 (rare, broken NAT) → priority 100 drop → check NAT chain
- Mode D "MTU mismatch": OVN 23.06+, gateway_mtu option set quá thấp → packet > MTU drop tại stage này → tăng option

**So sánh với hệ khác.** Linux router behavior: kernel drop packet có dst MAC khác NIC MAC ngay tại netif_receive_skb (trừ khi promisc) — tương đương priority 0 drop. Cisco IOS interface MAC validation analog. NSX-T DR (distributed router) admission stage gần giống hệt (cùng pattern declarative MAC + martian filter). Linux iptables `-m addrtype --src-type LOCAL` filter martian source tương đương priority 100.

---

## §13.19.8 LR_IN_IP_INPUT — xử lý packet hướng tới chính router

**Khái niệm.** `LR_IN_IP_INPUT` là stage logic **số 3** (OF table 11) — nơi xử lý packet **hướng tới chính router** (`ip.dst == <LRP_IP>`), thay vì packet quá cảnh router (forwarded). Xử lý gồm: trả lời ICMP echo (ping router), gửi ICMP TTL-exceeded, ICMP destination-unreachable cho fragment-needed (PMTUD), trả lời ARP/ND cho LRP IP, gửi BFD echo, và (tùy version) một phần routing protocol nhỏ. Loại: **pipeline stage cornerstone**, sub-loại "router self-traffic handler".

**Lịch sử + bối cảnh.** OVN 2.5 (2015) introduce Logical_Router với khả năng trả ICMP echo cơ bản. OVN 20.06 (2020) thêm fragment-needed (PMTUD) với action `icmp4_error`. OVN 21.03 (2021) thêm ARP/ND responder tích hợp tại stage này thay vì stage riêng (consolidate). OVN 22.03 (2022) tích hợp BFD echo native trong pipeline (trước đó BFD cần punt ra ovn-controller userspace). OVN 23.06 (2023) thêm hỗ trợ ICMP rate-limit để chống ICMP flood.

**Vị trí trong kiến trúc.** Stage logic 3 ⇒ OF table 11. Đứng sau `LR_IN_LOOKUP_NEIGHBOR` (logical 1) + `LR_IN_LEARN_NEIGHBOR` (logical 2), trước `LR_IN_DEFRAG` (logical 4). Scope: per-packet, chỉ packet có `eth.dst == <LRP_MAC> && ip.dst == <LRP_IP>` mới match priority cao tại đây; packet khác fall through priority 0 next sang stage routing.

**Vai trò.** Vai trò chính: **router self-service** — phản hồi tất cả packet đích đến router (ICMP, ARP cho LRP IP, BFD echo). Vai trò phụ: **error generator** — sinh ICMP error (TTL-exceeded từ stage routing trả về, destination-unreachable cho fragment-needed). Phạm vi ảnh hưởng: per-packet; có thể sinh thêm packet mới (reply) qua `clone` action.

**Vì sao sinh ra.** Linux router xử lý packet self-destination qua netfilter INPUT chain → kernel ICMP handler. OVN cần làm tương đương trong pipeline data plane để: (a) tránh punt mọi ping packet ra userspace (tốn kém), (b) đảm bảo PMTUD nhanh để tenant TCP không stuck với MTU sai, (c) BFD echo cần response trong < 1ms để health-check không false-down. Pain point cũ (Neutron-OVS + namespace router): mọi self-traffic phải qua kernel chain → slow. OVN inline trong pipeline → fast path datapath.

**Vấn đề giải quyết.** Cụ thể: trả lời packet đích router mà không cần punt ra userspace. Cách giải: hàm `build_lrouter_ipv4_ip_input` + `build_lrouter_ipv6_ip_input` (`northd/northd.c`) iterate mọi LRP, sinh flow priority cao match từng IP của LRP cho từng loại request:

- ICMP echo request → `clone { eth.src/dst swap; ip.src/dst swap; icmp4.type = 0; next; }` → reply ngay
- TTL = 1 → `icmp4_error` action sinh ICMP time-exceeded
- Fragment-needed → `icmp4_error` với type=3 code=4 + next-hop MTU
- ARP request có `arp.tpa == <LRP_IP>` → trả ARP reply với LRP MAC
- BFD echo destination = LRP IP → respond trong pipeline

Phạm vi giải quyết: chỉ self-traffic; forwarded traffic đi tiếp sang `LR_IN_DEFRAG` → `LR_IN_IP_ROUTING`.

**Importance.** A central pipeline stage.
