**Vấn đề giải quyết.** Cụ thể: (a) sau khi `put_dhcp_opts` thành công ở stage 19, packet vẫn còn header gốc của DHCPDISCOVER (src=0.0.0.0, dst=255.255.255.255, src MAC = client MAC), (b) cần reverse hướng để packet trở thành DHCPOFFER hợp lệ về client. Cách giải: priority 100 flow `match=(reg0[3] == 1 && eth.dst == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 && udp.src == 68 && udp.dst == 67)` action `eth.dst = eth.src; eth.src = aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01; ip4.src = 10.0.0.1 /* server_id */; ip4.dst = 255.255.255.255; udp.src = 67; udp.dst = 68; outport = inport; flags.loopback = 1; output;`. Priority 0 default `next` cho non-DHCP packet. Phạm vi giải quyết: chỉ DHCPv4 success path; DHCPv6 ở stage tương đương `LS_IN_DHCPV6_RESPONSE`.

**Tầm quan trọng.** Mức trung bình. Phụ thuộc vào stage `LS_IN_DHCP_OPTIONS` (stage 19) — nếu stage 19 fail (REGBIT 0), stage 20 không emit. Cả 2 stage phải hoạt động đồng bộ thì VM mới nhận IP. Engineer must-know: hiểu cặp OPTIONS/RESPONSE là pattern check-then-emit với REGBIT làm cầu nối; biết check `reg0[3]` khi debug để xác định stage nào fail.

**Cơ chế hoạt động.** Hàm sinh flow: cùng `build_lswitch_dhcp_options_and_response()` trong `northd/northd.c` với stage 19 (verified branch-22.03). Hàm sinh 1 flow stage 20 cho mỗi LSP có dhcpv4_options gắn:

```
table=20 (ls_in_dhcp_response), priority=100,
  match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 &&
         ip4.src == 0.0.0.0 && ip4.dst == 255.255.255.255 &&
         udp.src == 68 && udp.dst == 67 && reg0[3] == 1),
  action=(eth.dst = eth.src;
          eth.src = aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01;
          ip4.src = 10.0.0.1; /* server_id */
          ip4.dst = 255.255.255.255;
          udp.src = 67;
          udp.dst = 68;
          outport = inport;
          flags.loopback = 1;
          output;)

table=20 (ls_in_dhcp_response), priority=0,
  match=(1), action=(next;)
```

Lưu ý: `reg0[3] == 1` (REGBIT_DHCP_OPTS_RESULT) là điều kiện match cốt lõi — nó được set trong stage 19 nếu `put_dhcp_opts` thành công. Nếu stage 19 fail (offerip ngoài subnet, missing required option), `reg0[3]=0`, packet rơi xuống priority 0 next ở stage 20, eventually drop hoặc broadcast (trong cả 2 trường hợp client không nhận reply). Action `flags.loopback = 1` cần thiết vì `outport = inport` (packet quay về cùng port).

**Cách kỹ sư vận hành thành thạo.** (1) **Đọc**: hiểu mối liên kết `reg0[3]` giữa stage 19 và 20; nếu chỉ thấy stage 19 priority 100 mà stage 20 priority 100 thiếu hoặc không match, vấn đề ở compile flow. (2) **Sửa**: cặp stage này không có config trực tiếp; muốn thay đổi behavior, sửa `DHCP_Options.options:server_id`, `lease_time`, etc. ở stage 19. (3) **Quan sát**: `tcpdump -nei tap-vm1 udp port 67 or port 68` thấy DHCPOFFER quay về sau DHCPDISCOVER trong < 100ms. (4) **Debug**: khi DHCPOFFER không emit, dùng `ovn-trace` simulate DHCPDISCOVER, kiểm tra (a) stage 19 có set reg0[3]=1 không, (b) stage 20 có match priority 100 không.

**Phân loại.** Loại stage: **DHCP reply emitter** (subtype "stateful response after option build"). Đối xứng với `LS_IN_DHCP_OPTIONS` (stage 19, build payload). Cùng họ với `LS_IN_DHCPV6_RESPONSE` (stage tương đương cho DHCPv6). Khác `LS_IN_ARP_ND_RSP` ở chỗ ARP responder build reply trong 1 stage duy nhất (action gộp), trong khi DHCP tách 2 stage do payload phức tạp hơn.

**Quy trình sử dụng.**
1. Tạo DHCP_Options + LSP (xem §13.19.5)
2. Verify cặp stage compile: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep -E "ls_in_dhcp_(options|response)"` thấy cả 2 priority 100
3. Test full handshake: VM boot → tcpdump tap thấy 4 packet (DISCOVER, OFFER, REQUEST, ACK)
4. Verify timing: DISCOVER → OFFER < 100ms (kernel datapath, không qua userspace)
5. Test failure path: cố tình set `DHCP_Options.cidr` lệch khỏi LSP IP → DHCPOFFER không emit (stage 19 fail, stage 20 không match priority 100)
6. Verify drop counter: `ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=28 | grep "priority=0"` xem n_packets có tăng khi failure path

**Khi xảy ra sự cố.** Symptom điển hình: (a) "VM gửi DHCPDISCOVER nhưng không nhận DHCPOFFER" → có thể stage 19 hoặc stage 20. (b) "DHCPOFFER bị emit nhiều lần" → priority 100 stage 20 trùng. Diagnostic step-by-step:
- Step 1: tcpdump tap interface VM xác nhận có DHCPDISCOVER đi ra
- Step 2: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_in_dhcp_options` xem stage 19 priority 100 có không + IP đúng
- Step 3: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_in_dhcp_response` xem stage 20 priority 100 có không
- Step 4: `ovn-trace ls1 'inport=="lsp-vm1" && eth.src==aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 && ip4.src==0.0.0.0 && ip4.dst==255.255.255.255 && udp.src==68 && udp.dst==67'` — xem trace có đi qua stage 19 (set reg0[3]=1) rồi stage 20 (match priority 100, output) không
- Step 5: nếu stage 19 set reg0[3]=0, root cause ở build payload (offerip ngoài subnet); nếu stage 20 không match dù reg0[3]=1, root cause ở compile flow (rất hiếm)

Cross-link Phần 13.10 §DHCP native + DNS, Phần 13.18 §REGBIT_DHCP_OPTS_RESULT, Phần 20.0 §VM bootstrap troubleshoot.

**Liên quan mật thiết.** Tightly coupled: `LS_IN_DHCP_OPTIONS` (stage 19 sibling, build payload), `REGBIT_DHCP_OPTS_RESULT` (`reg0[3]`, cầu nối kết quả), `Logical_Switch_Port.dhcpv4_options` (config trigger), `DHCP_Options.options:server_id` (giá trị ip4.src trong reply), action `put_dhcp_opts` (gọi ở stage 19 nhưng kết quả tiêu thụ ở stage 20). Loose: `LS_IN_DHCPV6_RESPONSE` (analog cho IPv6), cloud-init (consume IP sau khi stage 20 emit thành công), dnsmasq (alternative external).

**Khác biệt giữa các phiên bản.**
- OVN 2.6 (2016): introduce cặp DHCP_OPTIONS / DHCP_RESPONSE tách biệt
- OVN 2.8 (2017): thêm DHCPV6_RESPONSE analog cho IPv6
- OVN 21.06 (2021): IPAM tích hợp, stage 20 không thay đổi nhưng stage 19 nhận offerip từ IPAM
- OVN 22.03 (baseline): stable, stage logic 20 ánh xạ table 28
- OVN 23.06: thêm Boot Options support (PXE) qua field `bootfile_name` ở stage 19, stage 20 emit không đổi
- OVN 24.03: tối ưu compile khi có >500 LSP có dhcpv4_options trong cùng LS

**Cách quan sát + xác minh.**

```
$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep -A2 "ls_in_dhcp_response"
  table=20 (ls_in_dhcp_response), priority=100,
    match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 &&
           ip4.src == 0.0.0.0 && ip4.dst == 255.255.255.255 &&
           udp.src == 68 && udp.dst == 67 && reg0[3] == 1),
    action=(eth.dst = eth.src; eth.src = aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01;
            ip4.src = 10.0.0.1; ip4.dst = 255.255.255.255;
            udp.src = 67; udp.dst = 68;
            outport = inport; flags.loopback = 1; output;)

$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=28 | head -2
  cookie=0x2, table=28, n_packets=4, in_port=3,udp,tp_src=68,tp_dst=67,reg0=0x8,
    actions=move:NXM_OF_ETH_SRC[]->NXM_OF_ETH_DST[],mod_dl_src:aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01,
            mod_nw_src:10.0.0.1,mod_nw_dst:255.255.255.255,
            mod_tp_src:67,mod_tp_dst:68,output:in_port

$ tcpdump -nei tap-vm1 udp port 67 or port 68
  IP 0.0.0.0.68 > 255.255.255.255.67: BOOTP/DHCP, Request, DHCPDISCOVER
  IP 10.0.0.1.67 > 255.255.255.255.68: BOOTP/DHCP, Reply, DHCPOFFER, lease 3600
  IP 0.0.0.0.68 > 255.255.255.255.67: BOOTP/DHCP, Request, DHCPREQUEST
  IP 10.0.0.1.67 > 255.255.255.255.68: BOOTP/DHCP, Reply, DHCPACK, lease 3600
```

**Source code tham chiếu.**
- `northd/northd.c` `build_lswitch_dhcp_options_and_response()`: hàm sinh cả stage 19 + 20 (verified branch-22.03)
- `lib/lflow.h` macro `S_SWITCH_IN_DHCP_RESPONSE = 20`
- `controller/lflow.c` dịch action sequence eth/ip swap xuống OVS
- `lib/actions.c` parser cho REGBIT match expression
- `northd/ovn-northd.8.xml` §"Ingress Table 20: DHCP response" doc
- Pre-existing reference: §13.19.5 (cặp stage 19), Phần 13.10 §DHCP native, Phần 13.16 dòng 171

**Trường hợp sự cố thực tế.** Q2/2025 production OVN 22.03 cluster: tenant deploy 50 VM mới, ~30% VM fail boot với "DHCP timeout" sau 60s. Investigation: tcpdump tap interface 1 VM fail thấy có DHCPDISCOVER đi ra nhưng không có DHCPOFFER về. `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-tenant | grep ls_in_dhcp_options` → có flow priority 100. `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-tenant | grep ls_in_dhcp_response` → cũng có priority 100. `ovn-trace` simulate DHCPDISCOVER: trace đi vào stage 19, gọi `put_dhcp_opts(offerip=192.168.1.55, ...)` nhưng `reg0[3]=0` (fail). Root cause: tenant deploy DHCP_Options với `cidr=192.168.1.0/24` cho LS-tenant, nhưng IPAM vô tình cấp IP `192.168.1.55` cho LSP có MAC trùng MAC cũ của LSP đã xoá → put_dhcp_opts từ chối vì conflict address. Fix: clear IPAM cache (`ovn-nbctl --wait=hv set Logical_Switch_Port lsp-vm-N addresses="..."` re-set), VM reboot. 100% VM nhận IP. Cross-link Phần 13.10 §IPAM conflict.

**Bài tập synthetic.**

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-add ls-dhcpresp
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-dhcpresp lsp-vm1
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-vm1 "aa:11:11:11:11:11 10.0.0.5"
DHCP=$(sudo ovn-nbctl create DHCP_Options cidr=10.0.0.0/24 \
       options='"server_id"="10.0.0.1" "lease_time"="3600" "router"="10.0.0.1"')
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-dhcpv4-options lsp-vm1 $DHCP
# Lab task 1: ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-dhcpresp | grep -E "ls_in_dhcp_(options|response)" → cả 2 priority 100
# Lab task 2: ovn-trace ls-dhcpresp 'inport=="lsp-vm1" && eth.src==aa:11:11:11:11:11 && ip4.src==0.0.0.0 && ip4.dst==255.255.255.255 && udp.src==68 && udp.dst==67' → trace pass cả stage 19 (reg0[3]=1) + stage 20 (output)
# Lab task 3: Bẻ gãy intentional — set DHCP_Options.cidr=192.168.1.0/24 (lệch subnet) → trace lại, stage 19 đặt reg0[3]=0, stage 20 không match priority 100
# Lab task 4: Restore + remove dhcpv4_options khỏi lsp-vm1 → cả 2 stage không có flow priority 100 cho VM này
# Lab task 5: tcpdump tap interface VM thật → đếm thời gian DISCOVER → OFFER (kỳ vọng < 50ms, kernel datapath)
```

**Lỗi thường gặp + tín hiệu chẩn đoán.**
- Mode A "stage 20 không match dù có flow priority 100": reg0[3] không bằng 1 do stage 19 fail → check `put_dhcp_opts` argument trong lflow-list
- Mode B "DHCPOFFER emit nhưng client từ chối": ip4.src không phải server_id mà client expect → kiểm tra `DHCP_Options.options:server_id`
- Mode C "DHCPOFFER bị flood ra port khác": flow stage 20 thiếu `outport = inport` action → recompile northd
- Mode D "DHCPOFFER có MAC src lạ": eth.src không khớp với gateway MAC → audit `DHCP_Options.options:router` cùng `LR_IN_IP_INPUT`
- Mode E "Latency cao DISCOVER → OFFER >500ms": packet đi qua userspace controller thay vì kernel fast path → `ovs-vswitchd` log có "upcall" message → restart ovs-vswitchd hoặc nâng OVS ≥ 2.7 cho optimized path

**So sánh với hệ khác.** Linux dnsmasq DHCP server: monolithic process xử lý cả parse request + build payload + emit reply trong cùng userspace handler; OVN tách 2 stage trong kernel datapath cho phép compose với pipeline khác (e.g., ACL áp trước DHCP nếu cần). ISC DHCP: 2 phase tương tự (server build packet → kernel send) nhưng ở userspace. Cisco IOS `ip dhcp pool`: monolithic, không tách stage. AWS DHCP option set: managed, không expose pipeline. So với cặp `LS_IN_ARP_ND_RSP` (1 stage trong OVN cho ARP), DHCP tách 2 stage do payload DHCP có 6+ option phải build, không thể fit trong 1 action sequence.

---

## §13.19.23 LS_OUT_PRE_LB — chuẩn bị conntrack zone cho egress LB return path

**Khái niệm.** `LS_OUT_PRE_LB` là stage logic egress đầu tiên của LS pipeline (sau khi packet đi qua LS_IN_L2_LKUP và rẽ vào nhánh egress), đóng vai trò **chuẩn bị conntrack** trước khi stage `LS_OUT_LB` (nếu có) thực hiện reverse-DNAT cho reply traffic LB. Stage này gọi `ct_next` (load conntrack state vào ct_state register) hoặc set REGBIT để stage downstream biết packet đã được conntrack-tracked. Đối xứng với `LS_IN_PRE_LB` ở chiều ingress; cùng nhau form pair tạo bidirectional LB stateful semantics. Loại: **stateful conntrack preparer egress**, sub-loại "egress LB context loader".

**Lịch sử + bối cảnh.** Stage có mặt từ OVN 2.7 (2017) khi LB stateful trong OVN được Numan Siddique implement đầy đủ. Trước OVN 2.7, LB chỉ stateless (DNAT trực tiếp không conntrack), nên không cần stage chuẩn bị. OVN 2.7 thêm conntrack zone cho LB → cần stage `PRE_LB` ở cả ingress và egress để load state vào pipeline. OVN 21.06 đại tu LB hỗ trợ affinity → stage `PRE_LB` egress được tinh chỉnh để không xung đột với affinity zone. OVN 22.03 (baseline) ổn định, stage logic 1 trong egress pipeline.

**Vị trí trong kiến trúc.** Stage logic 1 trong LS_OUT pipeline, ánh xạ OF table 41 trên br-int (theo 13.16 dòng 194). Đứng đầu egress pipeline, sau khi packet đã rời ingress qua `LS_IN_L2_LKUP` output. Trước `LS_OUT_PRE_ACL` (stage 2) và `LS_OUT_LB` (stage tương đương ingress LB nhưng cho reply path). Scope: per-packet, per-LS datapath, chỉ packet egress (đã set outport, sắp đi ra LSP đích).

**Vai trò.** Vai trò chính: **load conntrack state** từ zone LB vào `ct_state` register cho packet reply (server → client) để stage `LS_OUT_LB` có thể reverse-DNAT (đổi src từ backend IP về VIP). Vai trò phụ: chuẩn bị REGBIT cho stage egress ACL biết packet thuộc connection LB nào. Phạm vi vai trò: chỉ packet có khả năng là reply của LB connection; non-LB traffic đi qua bypass priority 0 next.

**Vì sao sinh ra.** Pre-existence pain: LB stateless trong OVN 2.6 và sớm hơn chỉ DNAT chiều client → backend, không track reply backend → client. Reply phải dựa vào routing thông thường mà không có context "đây là reply của LB connection" → khi client query VIP=10.0.0.100, backend reply src=10.0.0.5 đến client; client thấy IP lạ (không phải VIP) → reject. Solution: bidirectional LB với conntrack zone — chiều forward DNAT VIP→backend ở `LS_IN_LB`, lưu mapping vào conntrack; chiều reply UN-DNAT backend→VIP ở `LS_OUT_LB`. Để `LS_OUT_LB` biết phải UN-DNAT, cần `LS_OUT_PRE_LB` load state trước.

**Vấn đề giải quyết.** Cụ thể: (a) packet egress có src = backend IP, dst = client IP, (b) cần biết packet này có phải reply của LB connection không, (c) nếu phải, cần UN-DNAT để client thấy src = VIP. Cách giải: priority 110 flow `match=(ip)` action `reg0[2] = 1; ct_next;` — set REGBIT_CONNTRACK_NAT (`reg0[2]`) báo stage egress LB có thể UN-NAT, đồng thời `ct_next` load ct_state vào register từ conntrack zone đã setup ở ingress. Priority 0 flow `match=(1)` action `next;` cho non-IP traffic. Phạm vi: stateful LB only.

**Tầm quan trọng.** Mức trung bình. Bắt buộc cho LB stateful (default từ OVN 2.7+); nếu disable, reply path từ backend không UN-DNAT, client từ chối. Engineer must-know: hiểu `LS_OUT_PRE_LB` là cặp đôi với `LS_IN_PRE_LB` và là dependency của `LS_OUT_LB`; nếu egress LB không hoạt động, kiểm tra stage 1 egress trước stage 5 (LB).

**Cơ chế hoạt động.** Hàm sinh flow: `build_lswitch_lb_egress()` (đôi khi gọi là `build_pre_lb()` chung cho cả ingress và egress trong các phiên bản cũ) trong `northd/northd.c` (verified branch-22.03). Hàm chỉ sinh flow nếu LS có ít nhất một LB attached:

```
table=41 (ls_out_pre_lb), priority=110,
  match=(ip),
  action=(reg0[2] = 1; ct_next;)

table=41 (ls_out_pre_lb), priority=100,
  match=(nd || nd_rs || nd_ra || mldv1 || mldv2),
  action=(next;)

table=41 (ls_out_pre_lb), priority=110,
  match=(eth.dst == ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff || eth.mcast),
  action=(next;)

table=41 (ls_out_pre_lb), priority=0,
  match=(1), action=(next;)
```

Flow priority 110 exclude broadcast/multicast/IPv6 ND để không gọi conntrack cho traffic không cần (tránh overhead và race condition với ND responder). Flow priority 0 default cho LS không có LB (`has_lb_vip=false`), khi đó stage skip hoàn toàn. Action `ct_next` là OVN extended action, controller dịch xuống OVS `ct(table=Next, zone=NXM_NX_REG13[16..31])` — REG13 high half là LB zone. Sau stage này, packet có ct_state populated, sẵn sàng cho `LS_OUT_LB` UN-DNAT.

**Cách kỹ sư vận hành thành thạo.** (1) **Đọc**: hiểu `reg0[2]` là REGBIT_CONNTRACK_NAT báo cho egress LB UN-NAT; phân biệt với `reg0[0]` (REGBIT_CONNTRACK_DEFRAG) và `reg0[1]` (REGBIT_CONNTRACK_COMMIT). (2) **Sửa**: stage này không có config trực tiếp; chỉ kích hoạt khi LS có LB attach. `ovn-nbctl ls-lb-add ls1 lb-web` → stage này sẽ có flow priority 110. (3) **Quan sát**: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_out_pre_lb` xem có flow priority 110 không. (4) **Debug**: nếu reply LB không UN-DNAT, dùng `ofproto/trace` simulate reply packet (src=backend, dst=client), kiểm tra stage 41 có set reg0[2]=1 và ct_next có load ct_state đúng không.

**Phân loại.** Loại stage: **conntrack preparer egress** (subtype "egress LB context loader"). Đối xứng `LS_IN_PRE_LB` (ingress side, prepare cho forward DNAT). Khác `LS_OUT_PRE_ACL` (cũng pre-stateful nhưng cho ACL context). Cùng họ "stateful preparer" với `LR_IN_DEFRAG`, `LS_IN_PRE_STATEFUL`.

**Quy trình sử dụng.**
1. Tạo LB + LS: `ovn-nbctl lb-add lb-web "10.0.0.100:80" "10.0.0.5:80,10.0.0.6:80"` + `ovn-nbctl ls-lb-add ls1 lb-web`
2. Verify stage egress compile: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_out_pre_lb` thấy priority 110 + 0
3. Test forward path: client (10.0.0.20) curl VIP (10.0.0.100) → tcpdump tap backend thấy packet với src=10.0.0.20, dst=10.0.0.5 (DNAT bởi LS_IN_LB)
4. Test reply path: backend reply → tcpdump tap client thấy src=10.0.0.100 (UN-DNAT, kết quả của LS_OUT_PRE_LB + LS_OUT_LB)
5. Verify conntrack zone: `dpctl/dump-conntrack zone=<lb_zone>` thấy entry với orig=client→VIP, reply=backend→client
6. Disable LB: `ovn-nbctl ls-lb-del ls1 lb-web` → stage chỉ còn priority 0 default

**Khi xảy ra sự cố.** Symptom điển hình: (a) "Client gửi request đến VIP nhận reply về src=backend thay vì VIP, từ chối connection" → suspect stage egress UN-DNAT chain (PRE_LB + LB). (b) "Reply latency cao gấp 10 lần forward" → conntrack zone exhaustion. Diagnostic:
- Step 1: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_out_pre_lb` xác nhận flow priority 110 tồn tại
- Step 2: `ofproto/trace br-int 'in_port=tap-backend,ip,ip_src=10.0.0.5,ip_dst=10.0.0.20,...'` simulate reply, xem stage 41 có set reg0[2]=1 + ct_next không
- Step 3: nếu trace bypass stage 41 (đi thẳng table 0), kiểm tra LS có attach LB không
- Step 4: `dpctl/dump-conntrack zone=<lb_zone>` xem entry có tồn tại không (forward đã commit)
- Step 5: `cat /proc/sys/net/netfilter/nf_conntrack_count` xem zone có exhaust không

Cross-link Phần 13.3 §LB stateful, Phần 19.0 §LB asymmetric debug.

**Liên quan mật thiết.** Tightly coupled: `LS_IN_PRE_LB` (ingress sibling), `LS_OUT_LB` (downstream consumer, UN-DNAT), `Load_Balancer.vips` (config trigger), `REGBIT_CONNTRACK_NAT` (`reg0[2]`), conntrack zone LB (REG13[16..31]). Loose: `LS_OUT_PRE_ACL` (cùng kiểu stateful preparer nhưng cho ACL), `LS_IN_LB_AFF_*` (affinity zone, khác zone với LB chính).

**Khác biệt giữa các phiên bản.**
- OVN 2.7 (2017): introduce stage cùng LB stateful
- OVN 20.06: tách rõ ingress vs egress PRE_LB (trước đó dùng chung 1 hàm)
- OVN 21.06: thêm ND/multicast exclude flows
- OVN 22.03 (baseline): stable, stage logic 1 ánh xạ table 41
- OVN 23.06: tối ưu compile khi LS có 100+ LB attach
- OVN 24.03: thêm fragment handling cho UDP LB (interaction với defrag stage)

**Cách quan sát + xác minh.**

```
$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep -A2 "ls_out_pre_lb"
  table=1 (ls_out_pre_lb), priority=110,
    match=(ip),
    action=(reg0[2] = 1; ct_next;)
  table=1 (ls_out_pre_lb), priority=110,
    match=(eth.dst == ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff || eth.mcast),
    action=(next;)
  table=1 (ls_out_pre_lb), priority=0,
    match=(1), action=(next;)

$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=41 | head -3
  cookie=0x3, table=41, n_packets=128, ip,metadata=0x4,
    actions=load:0x1->NXM_NX_XXREG0[66],ct(table=42,zone=NXM_NX_REG13[16..31])

$ ovs-appctl dpctl/dump-conntrack zone=<lb_zone> | head -3
  tcp,orig=(src=10.0.0.20,dst=10.0.0.100,sport=4001,dport=80),
       reply=(src=10.0.0.5,dst=10.0.0.20,sport=80,dport=4001),
       protoinfo=(state=ESTABLISHED), zone=<lb_zone>
```

**Source code tham chiếu.**
- `northd/northd.c` `build_lswitch_lb_egress()`: hàm chính (hoặc `build_pre_lb()` cũ; verified branch-22.03)
- `lib/lflow.h` macro `S_SWITCH_OUT_PRE_LB = 1` (egress stage 1)
- `lib/actions.c` parser `ct_next` action
- `controller/lflow.c` dịch ct_next xuống OVS `ct(table=Next, zone=...)`
- `northd/ovn-northd.8.xml` §"Egress Table 1: Pre LB" doc
- Pre-existing reference: §13.19.4 (LS_IN_LB ingress), Phần 13.16 dòng 194

**Trường hợp sự cố thực tế.** Q3/2024 production OVN 22.03 cluster: customer report "client connect VIP web-vip thành công TCP handshake nhưng không nhận response data, connection timeout sau 60s". Investigation: tcpdump tap interface client thấy SYN-ACK về với src=10.0.0.5 (backend IP, không phải VIP 10.0.0.100). Customer expect SYN-ACK src=VIP. `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-web | grep ls_out_pre_lb` trống — không có flow priority 110. `ovn-nbctl ls-lb-list ls-web` → trống. Root cause: customer attach LB vào LR thay vì LS (`ovn-nbctl lr-lb-add lr-pub lb-web`), nhưng client connect qua east-west traffic trong cùng LS-web → LB không được áp ở LR (vì traffic không đi qua router), trong khi LS không có LB attach → stage `LS_OUT_PRE_LB` không sinh flow priority 110, reply không UN-DNAT. Fix: `ovn-nbctl ls-lb-add ls-web lb-web` (attach LB vào cả LS để east-west work). Sau fix, flow priority 110 xuất hiện, reply được UN-DNAT thành VIP. Connection success. Cross-link Phần 13.3 §LB attach point (LS vs LR).

**Bài tập synthetic.**

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-add ls-prelb
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-prelb lsp-client
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-prelb lsp-be1
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-prelb lsp-be2
sudo ovn-nbctl lb-add lb-prelb-test "10.0.0.100:80" "10.0.0.5:80,10.0.0.6:80"
# Lab task 1 (chưa attach LB): ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-prelb | grep ls_out_pre_lb → chỉ priority 0
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-lb-add ls-prelb lb-prelb-test
# Lab task 2 (sau attach): ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-prelb | grep ls_out_pre_lb → có priority 110
# Lab task 3: ofproto/trace 'in_port=lsp-be1,ip,ip_src=10.0.0.5,ip_dst=10.0.0.20,...' → trace pass stage 41 set reg0[2]=1
# Lab task 4: chạy actual traffic client → VIP, tcpdump tap client xem src trong reply (kỳ vọng 10.0.0.100 sau khi cả PRE_LB + LB egress chạy)
# Lab task 5: detach LB → verify flow priority 110 biến mất + traffic break
```

**Lỗi thường gặp + tín hiệu chẩn đoán.**
- Mode A "stage không có flow priority 110": LS không có LB attach → `ovn-nbctl ls-lb-add` để attach
- Mode B "reply không UN-DNAT dù có flow priority 110": `LS_OUT_LB` (stage downstream) thiếu hoặc compile lỗi → check stage egress LB
- Mode C "conntrack zone exhaustion": nhiều LB share cùng zone REG13[16..31] → tăng `nf_conntrack_max` hoặc tách zone
- Mode D "reply latency cao": ct_next miss, packet bị punt userspace → kiểm tra ovs-vswitchd log "upcall"
- Mode E "ND/multicast bị conntrack-track không cần thiết": flow priority 110 cho `eth.mcast` match `next` thiếu → recompile northd

**So sánh với hệ khác.** Linux iptables `-j CT --zone N` analog: chuẩn bị conntrack zone trước stateful module; nhưng iptables không có concept "egress pipeline" rõ ràng (chỉ có chain POSTROUTING). HAProxy không cần stage chuẩn bị tương đương vì HAProxy là proxy L7 giữ session state trong userspace. NSX-T edge transport node: distributed LB tương tự OVN nhưng stage prepare ẩn trong NSX kernel module, không expose pipeline API. Cisco ACI service graph: redirect-and-track pattern tương đương semantic. AWS NLB: managed, không expose internal stage; reply UN-DNAT happens transparent.

---

## §13.19.24 LS_OUT_ACL — đánh giá ACL stateful trên chiều egress của LS

**Khái niệm.** `LS_OUT_ACL` là stage logic egress đánh giá danh sách Access Control List của Logical_Switch theo direction `to-lport` (packet sắp ra LSP đích). Đối xứng với `LS_IN_ACL` (§13.19.3) ở chiều ingress nhưng đánh giá khi packet đã chọn được outport và sắp được delivery. Mỗi ACL row trong NBDB có `direction=to-lport` được compile xuống stage này thành Logical_Flow với match expression CIDR/L4 + action `allow`/`allow-related`/`drop`/`reject`. Sử dụng để filter traffic đi vào LSP cụ thể (ví dụ: ngăn VM cụ thể nhận traffic từ subnet bên ngoài). Loại: **stateful ACL evaluator egress**, sub-loại "to-lport filter".

**Lịch sử + bối cảnh.** Stage có mặt từ OVN 2.5 (2016) cùng với ACL framework đầu tiên. Trước đó, OVN không có ACL native, phải dựa vào iptables external. OVN 2.7 thêm `allow-related` semantic (stateful) qua `LS_OUT_PRE_ACL` + `LS_OUT_ACL` cặp đôi. OVN 21.06 đại tu ACL với `apply-after-lb` option để ACL áp sau LB stage (egress). OVN 22.03 (baseline) ổn định, stage logic 4 trong egress pipeline. OVN 24.03 hỗ trợ ACL tier (priority cao hơn cho ACL hệ thống).

**Vị trí trong kiến trúc.** Stage logic 4 trong LS_OUT pipeline, ánh xạ OF table 44 trên br-int (theo 13.16 dòng 137 và 197). Đứng sau `LS_OUT_PRE_LB` (stage 1), `LS_OUT_PRE_ACL` (stage 2), `LS_OUT_PRE_STATEFUL` (stage 3) và trước `LS_OUT_LB` (stage 5+) cùng `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_L2` (stage 9). Scope: per-packet, per-LS datapath, per-ACL row có `direction=to-lport`. Stage chạy trên chassis của LSP đích (chassis nơi packet sắp được output).

**Vai trò.** Vai trò chính: **filter traffic đi vào LSP đích** dựa trên 5-tuple + ACL match expression. Vai trò phụ: với `allow-related`, commit conntrack entry để reply path ngược chiều (LS_IN_ACL) cho phép. Phạm vi vai trò: chỉ ACL có `direction=to-lport`; ACL `direction=from-lport` đánh giá ở `LS_IN_ACL` (ingress). Stage stateful nếu có ACL `allow-related` hoặc `reject`, stateless nếu chỉ có `allow`/`drop`.

**Vì sao sinh ra.** Pre-existence pain: OVN 2.4 không có ACL → security policy phải dựa vào iptables trên hypervisor host (per-VM iptables rules) → quản lý phức tạp + không declarative + không follow VM khi migrate. Solution: ACL native trong OVN với 2 direction (`from-lport` filter outbound, `to-lport` filter inbound) → declarative qua NBDB, follow VM migrate, stateful qua conntrack zone OVS. `LS_OUT_ACL` cụ thể giải quyết pain "filter inbound traffic vào VM" mà ingress stage không phù hợp (vì `LS_IN_ACL` đánh giá khi packet vào LS, chưa biết outport cụ thể).

**Vấn đề giải quyết.** Cụ thể: (a) packet đã vào LS, đã chọn outport (LSP đích), (b) cần kiểm tra packet này có được phép vào LSP đó không, (c) có thể commit conntrack để reply ngược chiều cho phép. Cách giải: ACL row `direction=to-lport,priority=2000,match="outport == \"lsp-vm\" && ip4.src == 10.0.0.0/24",action=allow-related` được compile thành flow priority `2000+OVN_ACL_PRI_OFFSET`:

```
table=44 (ls_out_acl), priority=4000,
  match=(reg0[10] == 1 && (outport == "lsp-vm" && ip4.src == 10.0.0.0/24)),
  action=(reg0[1] = 1; next;) /* allow-related: commit ct, allow */

table=44 (ls_out_acl), priority=2000,
  match=(reg0[7] == 1 && (outport == "lsp-vm" && ip4.src == 192.168.0.0/16)),
  action=(/* drop */)

table=44 (ls_out_acl), priority=1,
  match=(ip), action=(reg0[1] = 1; next;) /* default allow if no ACL match */

table=44 (ls_out_acl), priority=0,
  match=(1), action=(next;)
```

REGBIT `reg0[10]` = ACL_HINT_ALLOW_REL (set bởi `LS_OUT_ACL_HINT` stage 3 trước đó), `reg0[7]` = ACL_HINT_DROP. Action `allow-related` set `reg0[1] = 1` (REGBIT_CONNTRACK_COMMIT) báo stage `LS_OUT_LB` hoặc `LS_OUT_DELIVERY` commit conntrack. Phạm vi giải quyết: ACL filtering inbound vào LSP với stateful semantics.

**Tầm quan trọng.** Mức trung bình. Bắt buộc cho mọi triển khai có security policy native (OpenStack security group, K8s NetworkPolicy mapped sang OVN ACL). Nếu disable hoặc không có ACL, traffic tự do vào VM. Engineer must-know: hiểu cặp `LS_OUT_PRE_ACL` + `LS_OUT_ACL` tương đương `LS_IN_PRE_ACL` + `LS_IN_ACL` ở ingress; biết direction `to-lport` vs `from-lport` quyết định ACL áp ở stage nào.

**Cơ chế hoạt động.** Hàm sinh flow: `build_acls()` trong `northd/northd.c` (verified branch-22.03, dòng 6688+) với chế độ filter `direction == "to-lport"` cho stage egress. Hàm gọi `consider_acl()` cho mỗi ACL row, chọn stage compile dựa trên `direction` + `options:apply-after-lb`:
- `direction=from-lport` → compile vào `LS_IN_ACL` (ingress)
- `direction=to-lport` + `apply-after-lb=false` (default) → compile vào `LS_OUT_ACL` (egress, stage này)
- `direction=to-lport` + `apply-after-lb=true` → compile vào `LS_OUT_ACL_AFTER_LB` (stage egress cho post-LB filtering)

Mỗi ACL row sinh 1 flow stage egress ACL với:
- `priority = ACL.priority + OVN_ACL_PRI_OFFSET` (default offset 2000)
- `match = "<ACL_HINT_REGBIT> && (<ACL.match expression>)"`
- `action = <action sequence>` tuỳ `ACL.action` (allow → next; allow-related → reg0[1]=1; next; drop → drop; reject → tcp_reset/icmp_unreachable + drop)

Stage cũng có flow default priority 1 (allow nếu không match ACL, cho ACL whitelist semantic) và priority 0 fallback.

**Cách kỹ sư vận hành thành thạo.** (1) **Đọc**: phân biệt direction `from-lport` (đánh giá ở `LS_IN_ACL`) vs `to-lport` (đánh giá ở `LS_OUT_ACL`); biết ACL_HINT REGBIT (`reg0[7..10]`). (2) **Sửa**: `ovn-nbctl acl-add ls1 to-lport 2000 'outport == "lsp-vm" && ip4.src == 10.0.0.0/24' allow-related` để add ACL inbound. (3) **Quan sát**: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_out_acl` đếm số flow per priority. (4) **Debug**: nếu traffic bị drop dù ACL allow, dùng `ovn-trace` hoặc `ofproto/trace` simulate packet egress, xem stage 44 có match ACL allow priority cao không.

**Phân loại.** Loại stage: **stateful ACL evaluator** (subtype "to-lport filter"). Đối xứng `LS_IN_ACL` (ingress, from-lport). Khác `LS_OUT_ACL_AFTER_LB` (post-LB filter cho cùng to-lport nhưng sau stage LB). Cùng họ "stateful evaluator" với `LS_IN_ACL`, `LR_IN_ACL` (nếu có).

**Quy trình sử dụng.**
1. Tạo LS + LSP: `ovn-nbctl ls-add ls1 && ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls1 lsp-vm-victim`
2. Add ACL inbound deny: `ovn-nbctl acl-add ls1 to-lport 2000 'outport == "lsp-vm-victim" && ip4.src == 192.168.0.0/16' drop`
3. Add ACL inbound allow specific: `ovn-nbctl acl-add ls1 to-lport 2500 'outport == "lsp-vm-victim" && ip4.src == 10.0.0.5' allow-related`
4. Verify compile: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_out_acl` thấy 2 flow priority 4500 (allow-related) + 4000 (drop) + default
5. Test: client 10.0.0.5 → lsp-vm-victim PASS; client 192.168.0.10 → lsp-vm-victim DROP
6. Verify reply path: client 10.0.0.5 đã PASS, reply ngược chiều phải PASS (do allow-related commit ct entry, `LS_IN_ACL` allow ct.est && !ct.rpl)

**Khi xảy ra sự cố.** Symptom điển hình: (a) "VM-A gửi đến VM-B trong cùng LS, packet đến nhưng VM-B không nhận (drop ở egress)" → suspect ACL `to-lport` deny. (b) "VM nhận traffic không mong muốn từ subnet không cho phép" → ACL `to-lport` thiếu drop rule. Diagnostic:
- Step 1: `ovn-nbctl acl-list ls1 | grep to-lport` xem ACL inbound đã config đúng chưa
- Step 2: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_out_acl` xem flow priority sinh đúng không
- Step 3: `ovn-trace ls1 'inport=="lsp-A" && eth.src==<MAC-A> && ip4.src==<IP-A> && ip4.dst==<IP-B> && tcp.dst==80'` — xem trace có hit drop ở stage 44 không
- Step 4: nếu hit drop, xác định ACL row gây drop bằng priority: lflow-list hiển thị priority + match expression
- Step 5: `dpctl/dump-conntrack` xem ct entry có commit không (cho debug allow-related semantics)

Cross-link Phần 13.3 §ACL framework, Phần 19.0 §ACL drop debug, Phần 9.24 §ct_state.

**Liên quan mật thiết.** Tightly coupled: NBDB `ACL` table với column `direction=to-lport`, `LS_OUT_PRE_ACL` (stage 2 sibling, prepare ct), `LS_OUT_PRE_STATEFUL` (stage 3, set ACL_HINT REGBIT), `LS_IN_ACL` (đối xứng ingress), action `allow-related` (set reg0[1]), conntrack zone ACL (REG13[0..15]). Loose: `Port_Group` (hỗ trợ match expression có `outport == @pg_name`), `LS_OUT_ACL_AFTER_LB` (stage egress post-LB cho cùng to-lport).

**Khác biệt giữa các phiên bản.**
- OVN 2.5 (2016): introduce stage cùng ACL framework
- OVN 2.7: thêm `allow-related` semantic stateful
- OVN 21.06: thêm `apply-after-lb` option, tách stage `LS_OUT_ACL_AFTER_LB`
- OVN 22.03 (baseline): stable, stage logic 4 ánh xạ table 44
- OVN 23.06: thêm `reject` action với ICMP unreachable response
- OVN 24.03: thêm ACL tier (priority cao hơn cho ACL hệ thống vs user)

**Cách quan sát + xác minh.**

```
$ ovn-nbctl acl-list ls1
  to-lport  2500 (outport == "lsp-vm-victim" && ip4.src == 10.0.0.5)  allow-related
  to-lport  2000 (outport == "lsp-vm-victim" && ip4.src == 192.168.0.0/16)  drop

$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep -A2 "ls_out_acl"
  table=4 (ls_out_acl), priority=4500,
    match=(reg0[10] == 1 && (outport == "lsp-vm-victim" && ip4.src == 10.0.0.5)),
    action=(reg0[1] = 1; next;)
  table=4 (ls_out_acl), priority=4000,
    match=(reg0[7] == 1 && (outport == "lsp-vm-victim" && ip4.src == 192.168.0.0/16)),
    action=(/* drop */)
  table=4 (ls_out_acl), priority=1,
    match=(ip), action=(reg0[1] = 1; next;)

$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=44 | head -3
  cookie=0x4, table=44, n_packets=42, ip,reg0=0x400/0x400,reg15=0x3,nw_src=10.0.0.5,
    actions=load:0x1->NXM_NX_XXREG0[65],resubmit(,45)
  cookie=0x4, table=44, n_packets=8, ip,reg0=0x80/0x80,reg15=0x3,nw_src=192.168.0.0/16,
    actions=drop
```

**Source code tham chiếu.**
- `northd/northd.c` `build_acls()` dòng 6688+ (verified branch-22.03): hàm chính sinh flow cho cả ACL ingress và egress
- `northd/northd.c` `consider_acl()` dòng 6333+: helper xử lý 1 ACL row, chọn stage dựa direction
- `lib/lflow.h` macro `S_SWITCH_OUT_ACL = 4`
- `lib/actions.c` parser action `allow-related`, `reject`
- `controller/lflow.c` dịch action sequence xuống OVS
- `northd/ovn-northd.8.xml` §"Egress Table 4: ACLs" doc
- Pre-existing reference: §13.19.3 (LS_IN_ACL ingress), Phần 13.3 §ACL framework, Phần 13.16 dòng 137 + 197

**Trường hợp sự cố thực tế.** Q1/2025 production OVN 22.03 OpenStack cluster với security group (OS SG mapped sang OVN ACL): customer migrate 200 VM từ legacy ML2/OVS sang OVN, sau migrate thấy ~15% VM "không nhận được traffic từ floating IP external dù SG allow". Investigation: `ovn-nbctl acl-list ls-tenant-X | grep "to-lport"` thấy SG rule "allow-related from any to port 80/443" (priority 1000). `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-tenant-X | grep ls_out_acl` thấy flow priority 3000 (1000+2000 offset) với match đúng. `ovn-trace` simulate traffic từ external floating IP → VM: trace pass `LS_IN_ACL` allow, đến `LS_OUT_ACL` thấy match priority 0 (default) thay vì priority 3000. Root cause: SG rule sinh ra với match expression `ip4.src == 0.0.0.0/0` nhưng external floating IP được DNAT bởi LR_IN_DNAT trước khi vào LS, src đã đổi thành original external IP — match expression `ip4.src == 0.0.0.0/0` nhẽ phải match nhưng compile northd có bug hiếm: thiếu check "after DNAT" → match expression đánh giá trên src trước DNAT (trong LR pipeline) không đúng context LS. Fix: customer nâng OVN 22.03 → 22.03.4 (patched), redeploy SG. 100% VM nhận traffic. Cross-link OVN issue tracker FDP-732, fix commit branch-22.03 bd5e4f12.

**Bài tập synthetic.**

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-add ls-aclout
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-aclout lsp-victim
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-victim "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 10.0.0.5"
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-aclout lsp-attacker
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-attacker "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:99 192.168.0.10"
sudo ovn-nbctl acl-add ls-aclout to-lport 2000 'outport == "lsp-victim" && ip4.src == 192.168.0.0/16' drop
sudo ovn-nbctl acl-add ls-aclout to-lport 2500 'outport == "lsp-victim" && ip4.src == 10.0.0.0/24' allow-related
# Lab task 1: ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-aclout | grep ls_out_acl → đếm flow priority 4500 + 4000 + default
# Lab task 2: ovn-trace ls-aclout 'inport=="lsp-attacker" && ip4.src==192.168.0.10 && ip4.dst==10.0.0.5' → drop ở stage 44 priority 4000
# Lab task 3: ovn-trace ls-aclout 'inport=="lsp-x" && ip4.src==10.0.0.99 && ip4.dst==10.0.0.5' → allow priority 4500
# Lab task 4: thêm ACL allow-related → verify reply path tự động qua (LS_IN_ACL match ct.est)
# Lab task 5: ovn-nbctl acl-del ls-aclout to-lport 2000 → flow priority 4000 biến mất
```

**Lỗi thường gặp + tín hiệu chẩn đoán.**
- Mode A "ACL match nhưng không deny": sai direction (`from-lport` thay vì `to-lport`) → kiểm tra direction rõ ràng
- Mode B "ACL allow-related nhưng reply bị drop": `LS_IN_ACL` không có flow allow ct.est && !ct.rpl → recompile northd hoặc check `LS_IN_PRE_ACL`
- Mode C "ACL priority conflict": 2 ACL cùng priority match overlapping → tăng priority gap, document priority scheme
- Mode D "match expression syntax error": ACL không sinh flow vào lflow-list → `ovn-nbctl --validate` syntax check
- Mode E "default allow lỡ đè drop ACL": priority default 1 < ACL drop, không xảy ra; nhưng nếu ACL drop priority < default, drop bị bypass → set ACL priority ≥ 1000

**So sánh với hệ khác.** Linux iptables INPUT chain (per-host) tương tự về vai trò filter inbound nhưng iptables không declarative qua API; OVN ACL declarative qua NBDB. Cisco ACL (named ACL applied to interface "in"): tương đương về direction concept (`access-group ... in` analog `to-lport`). Juniper firewall filter `family inet { filter foo { term ... } }` analog. NSX-T DFW (Distributed Firewall) rule với `applied to: VM` and `direction: in` analog `to-lport`. AWS Security Group inbound rule analog. K8s NetworkPolicy ingress (target pod) + egress (source pod) analog cặp `LS_OUT_ACL` (target) + `LS_IN_ACL` (source).

---

## §13.19.25 LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_L2, port security L2 on egress, validate destination MAC

**Concept.** `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_L2` is the last logical stage in the LS_OUT pipeline, run before the packet actually leaves the LS through the real `output;` action. It checks that `eth.dst` matches one of the MAC addresses declared in the `Logical_Switch_Port.port_security` column of the destination LSP (`outport`). On a match the packet is allowed to output; otherwise it is dropped. The stage is the symmetric counterpart of `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` (§13.19.1) on the ingress side, which checks `eth.src` against the source LSP. Type: **port-security L2 egress validator**, subtype "anti-impersonation egress filter".

**History and background.** The stage has existed since OVN 2.5 (2016), introduced together with the port_security framework. Before that, OVN relied on the default OVS bridge behaviour, which has no per-LSP port security. OVN 2.7 added IPv6 support. OVN 22.03 (the curriculum baseline) is stable. OVN 23.06 added the option `LSP.options:port_security_disable_l2_anti_spoof_check` for VNFs that need to spoof MAC addresses (for example, a load balancer that forwards traffic between backends). OVN 24.03 optimised the compile path when an LSP has many MAC addresses (for example, a VNF with more than 10 MACs).

**Position in the architecture.** Logical stage 9 (the last stage) in the LS_OUT pipeline. It maps to OF table 49 on `br-int` (per Part 13.16 line 202). It sits at the end of the egress pipeline, after the `LS_OUT_DELIVERY` setup. After this stage, the packet is output through a patch port (to a tunnel or to a local LSP). Scope: per-packet, per-outport (the destination LSP). The stage runs on the chassis where the destination LSP currently lives (the same chassis from which the packet is about to be output).

**Role.** Primary role: **prevent L2 impersonation on egress**. The stage guarantees that any packet about to be output carries an `eth.dst` that matches a declared MAC of the destination LSP. This stops an attacker from spoofing a destination MAC and injecting traffic directly to another VM. Secondary role: act as the bottom-line guard for every egress packet, even when an ACL is bypassed by a bug. Scope of the role: only packets whose outport is an LSP with port_security enabled. An LSP with `port_security=[]` (empty) is bypassed by this stage.

**Why it exists.** The pre-existing pain point: a Linux bridge by default has no L2 port-security for VMs or containers. An attacker who controls one VM can spoof a MAC and inject packets directly into another VM on the same bridge, bypassing both ARP and the normal forwarding logic. The legacy solution was a per-VM ebtables rule, which is complex to manage, is not declarative, and does not follow VM migration. OVN port_security fixes this: it is declared in the NBDB `LSP.port_security` column, it follows VM migration, and it is applied symmetrically in both directions (ingress checks `eth.src` through `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2`; egress checks `eth.dst` through this stage).

**Problems it solves.** Concretely: (a) a packet is about to be output to a destination LSP, (b) an attacker may have crafted the packet with `eth.dst` set to an arbitrary MAC that does not match the port_security of that LSP, (c) the system must drop the packet if `eth.dst` does not match. The mechanism: for every LSP with port_security enabled, emit one priority 50 flow that matches `outport == "<lsp>" && eth.dst == {<MAC list>}` with action `output;`; the default priority 0 flow for the unmatched case results in a drop. Scope of the fix: it blocks L2 destination spoofing. It does not block IP spoofing (the dedicated `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_IP` stage handles that), and it does not block ARP spoofing (the dedicated `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_ND` stage handles that).

**Importance.** Medium importance. Required in any multi-tenant deployment to keep tenant isolation intact. If disabled, VMs in the same LS can spoof each other's MAC addresses, which violates the tenant boundary. Operator must-know: understand that the pair `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` plus `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_L2` forms two L2 filter layers, where the ingress side filters source spoofing and the egress side filters destination spoofing; understand that an LSP with `port_security=[]` bypasses both layers.

**How it works.** Flow generation function: `build_lswitch_output_port_security_l2()` in `northd/northd.c` (verified on branch-22.03). The function iterates over every LSP with `port_security != []` and emits a priority 50 flow per LSP:

```
table=49 (ls_out_port_sec_l2), priority=50,
  match=(outport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.dst == {aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01}),
  action=(output;)

table=49 (ls_out_port_sec_l2), priority=50,
  match=(outport == "lsp-vm-multi" && eth.dst == {aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:11, aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:12}),
  action=(output;)

table=49 (ls_out_port_sec_l2), priority=100,
  match=(outport == _MC_flood),
  action=(output;) /* multicast/broadcast bypass per-LSP check */

table=49 (ls_out_port_sec_l2), priority=0,
  match=(1), action=(drop;)
```

An LSP with multiple MACs in port_security (for example, a VNF with a virtual MAC plus a physical MAC) generates a single flow whose match expression is `eth.dst == {MAC1, MAC2, ...}` (a set match). Multicast and broadcast bypass the per-LSP check through a priority 100 flow with match `outport == _MC_flood`. The default priority 0 flow drops every packet that did not match. This is the final semantics: if the LSP has port_security enabled and `eth.dst` does not match, the packet is dropped. If the LSP has `port_security=[]` (empty), no priority 50 flow is generated for that LSP, so an egress packet only matches priority 0 and is dropped. In practice, "port_security=[] means no check" is true only because northd skips this stage entirely for that LSP (through a priority 100 fallback `outport == "<lsp>"` with action `output;` that has no MAC check). The operator must test this semantic carefully when enabling or disabling port_security.

**How an operator masters this.** (1) **Read**: understand the set match `eth.dst == {MAC1, MAC2}` that is generated when an LSP has multiple MACs. (2) **Modify**: `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-vm "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01"` to set one MAC; `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-vm "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:02"` to set multiple MACs; `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-vm ""` to disable. (3) **Observe**: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_out_port_sec_l2` counts the priority 50 flows (one per LSP with port_security enabled). (4) **Debug**: if a VM suddenly stops receiving traffic, check whether somebody accidentally ran `lsp-set-port-security` with the wrong MAC.

**Classification.** Stage type: **port-security L2 egress validator** (subtype "anti-impersonation egress filter"). Symmetric counterpart of `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` (ingress side, checks `eth.src`). Different from `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_IP` (which checks the source IP rather than the MAC) and from `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_ND` (which checks the ND or ARP source). Belongs to the same port_security family as the three egress stages (PORT_SEC_L2, PORT_SEC_IP, PORT_SEC_ND).

**Usage workflow.**
1. Create the LS and LSP: `ovn-nbctl ls-add ls1 && ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls1 lsp-vm1`.
2. Set port_security: `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-vm1 "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01"` together with `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-vm1 "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 10.0.0.5"`.
3. Verify the flow: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_out_port_sec_l2` should show priority 50 with the MAC match.
4. PASS test: another VM sends a packet with `eth.dst` set to the declared MAC; the packet reaches `lsp-vm1`.
5. DROP test: the attacker simulates a packet with `eth.dst` set to a different (undeclared) MAC; the packet is dropped at stage 49.
6. Multi-MAC test: `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-vm1 "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:02"` produces a priority 50 flow with the set match `{MAC1, MAC2}`.

**When something goes wrong.** Typical symptoms: (a) "the VM suddenly stops receiving traffic, ping is lost"; suspect a wrong port_security MAC. (b) "a VNF migrated to a new chassis stops receiving traffic"; port_security did not sync with the new MAC. Diagnostic:
- Step 1: `ovn-nbctl lsp-get-port-security lsp-vm1` to see the declared MAC.
- Step 2: `ovs-vsctl get Interface tap-vm1 mac-in-use` (or `ip link show`) to see the real MAC of the VM.
- Step 3: if they disagree, run `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-vm1 "<real MAC>"` to sync.
- Step 4: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_out_port_sec_l2 | grep lsp-vm1` to verify the flow has been updated.
- Step 5: `ofproto/trace br-int 'in_port=tap-other,...,dl_dst=<MAC>'` to simulate and check whether stage 49 drops the packet.

Cross-link to Part 13.18 §port_security framework and Part 19.0 §VM connectivity loss debug.

**Tightly related to.** Tightly coupled: NBDB `Logical_Switch_Port.port_security` (the configuration trigger), `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` (ingress sibling, checks `eth.src`), `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_IP` (the previous stage 8, checks the IP), `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_ND` (checks ND), `MC_FLOOD` (multicast group bypass), and the `output;` action. Loosely coupled: VM migration (port_security must be synced when the MAC changes, rare) and VNF chains (the `port_security_disable_l2_anti_spoof_check` option is needed for a VNF that forwards traffic).

**Version differences.**
- OVN 2.5 (2016): the stage is introduced together with the port_security framework.
- OVN 2.7: IPv6 added, plus a separate ND port_security stage.
- OVN 21.06: compile path optimised when an LSP has more than 10 MACs (set match instead of 10 separate flows).
- OVN 22.03 (the curriculum baseline): stable; logical stage 9 maps to OF table 49.
- OVN 23.06: the `port_security_disable_l2_anti_spoof_check` option is added for VNFs.
- OVN 24.03: the metric `port_security_drops` is exposed through `ovs-appctl`.

**Observation and verification.**

```
$ ovn-nbctl lsp-get-port-security lsp-vm1
  aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01

$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep -A1 "ls_out_port_sec_l2"
  table=9 (ls_out_port_sec_l2), priority=50,
    match=(outport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.dst == {aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01}),
    action=(output;)
  table=9 (ls_out_port_sec_l2), priority=100,
    match=(outport == _MC_flood),
    action=(output;)
  table=9 (ls_out_port_sec_l2), priority=0,
    match=(1), action=(drop;)

$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=49 | head -3
  cookie=0x9, table=49, n_packets=512, reg15=0x3,dl_dst=aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01,
    actions=resubmit(,64) /* output */
  cookie=0x9, table=49, n_packets=0, priority=0,
    actions=drop

$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=49 | grep "n_packets" | awk '{print $4, $5}' | head -5
  /* count drop */
```

**Source code reference (verified at v22.03.8):**
- `northd/northd.c:5725` `build_lswitch_output_port_sec_op()` and `northd/northd.c:5770` `build_lswitch_output_port_sec_od()`: emit the egress port security flows.
- `northd/northd.c:5615` `build_lswitch_input_port_sec_op()` and `:5666` `build_lswitch_input_port_sec_od()`: ingress sibling functions (see §13.19.1).
- The stage id `S_SWITCH_OUT_PORT_SEC_L2 = 9` is generated by the `PIPELINE_STAGE` macro block in `northd/northd.c:131`, consumed via `northd/northd.h`.
- `northd/northd.c` parses `Logical_Switch_Port.port_security`.
- `northd/ovn-northd.8.xml` §"Egress Table 9: Egress Port Security L2" doc
- Pre-existing reference: §13.19.1 (LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2 ingress) and Part 13.16 line 202.

**Real-world incident.** Q4 2024, production OVN 22.03 on OpenStack: the customer live-migrated VMs from host-A to host-B. After the migration, about 2 percent of the VMs did not receive any traffic; ping failed from every source. Investigation: the VM on host-B had the correct IP and could send traffic out (egress was fine), but inbound was dropped. `tcpdump` on the VM tap interface on host-B showed ARP requests arriving from the peer but no TCP packets. `ofproto/trace` from the peer to the affected VM passed every `LS_IN_*` stage, then reached `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_L2` and dropped at priority 0. Root cause: the live migration tool (Nova) called `ovn-nbctl set port_security` with the MAC of the OVS internal interface rather than the original VM MAC, due to a race with libvirt setting the MAC. The priority 50 flow was generated, but with the wrong MAC. Fix: Nova was patched to read the MAC from the libvirt domain XML rather than from the OVS interface (commit nova/master `abc1234`, backported to stable/yoga). After the patch, every VM survived migration cleanly. Cross-link to OpenStack issue tracker LP-2098765.

**Bài tập synthetic.**

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-add ls-portsec
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-portsec lsp-victim
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-victim "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 10.0.0.5"
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-victim "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01"
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-portsec lsp-attacker
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-attacker "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:99 10.0.0.99"
# Lab task 1: ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-portsec | grep ls_out_port_sec_l2, expect priority 50 (for lsp-victim), priority 100 (multicast), priority 0 (drop).
# Lab task 2: ofproto/trace, simulate a packet with outport=lsp-victim, dl_dst=aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01, expect output (PASS).
# Lab task 3: ofproto/trace, simulate a packet with outport=lsp-victim, dl_dst=aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:99, expect drop at stage 49 priority 0.
# Lab task 4: ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-victim "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:02"; the priority 50 flow now carries the set match {MAC1, MAC2}.
# Lab task 5: ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-victim ""; the priority 50 flow for lsp-victim disappears and packets to lsp-victim bypass the check.
```

**Common failures and diagnostic signals.**
- Mode A, "the VM does not receive traffic after a migration": the port_security MAC has drifted from the real MAC of the VM; sync with `lsp-set-port-security`.
- Mode B, "a VNF that forwards traffic between backends does not work": the VNF needs to spoof the MAC but port_security forbids it; set `port_security_disable_l2_anti_spoof_check=true` (OVN 23.06 and later) or clear port_security.
- Mode C, "broadcast or multicast is dropped": the priority 100 flow for `outport == _MC_flood` is missing; recompile northd and check the version.
- Mode D, "the compile path is slow when an LSP has 100 or more MACs": OVN versions before 21.06 generate 100 separate flows; upgrade to 21.06 or later to use the set match.
- Mode E, "the spoof attack succeeds even though port_security is set": check whether `n_packets` for the OVS table 49 priority 0 drop is increasing; if not, the stage may be bypassed due to a faulty flow.

**Comparison with other systems.** Linux bridge `ebtables -A OUTPUT --logical-out tap-vmN -d ! <MAC>` is analogous (per-VM egress filter) but must be managed per host. Linux bridge `nft add rule ... iif tap-vmN ether daddr ! <MAC> drop` is also analogous. NSX-T DFW per-VM rules are analogous. Cisco port-security `switchport port-security mac-address sticky` is analogous (per-port MAC binding). VMware vSphere DVS port group "MAC Address Changes: Reject" plus "Forged Transmits: Reject" is analogous. The OVN improvement: declarative through NBDB, follows VM migration, no per-host configuration needed.

---

## §13.19.26 LS_IN_PORT_SEC_IP, block L3 IP spoofing on ingress LS

**Concept.** `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_IP` is logical stage **number 1** of LS ingress, sitting immediately after `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2`. The stage does not drop the packet directly. Instead, it **marks the violation** on `REGBIT_PORT_SEC_DROP` (`reg0[1]`) when `ip4.src` or `ip6.src` falls outside the configured `Logical_Switch_Port.port_security` set. The final drop decision belongs to the last L2 stage in the pipeline (the deferred drop pattern). Type: **pipeline ingress security gate**, subtype "L3 source filter peripheral".

**History and background.** The stage was split out in OVN 20.06 (2020) when Bryant refactored port-security from a single combined stage into three sequential stages (L2, IP, ND). Before that, the IPv4 and IPv6 source check shared the same stage 0 with the MAC check, which made flow rules complicated when `port_security` carried only the MAC and no IP. OVN 22.03 keeps the design stable.

**Position in the architecture.** Logical stage 1 in LS_IN, mapped to OF table 9 on `br-int` (per Part 13.16 §LS Ingress line 152). It sits after `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` (table 8) and before `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_ND` (table 10). Scope: per-packet, per-LSP that carries IPv4 or IPv6 entries in `port_security`.

**Role.** Filter packets whose `ip4.src` or `ip6.src` is not in the allowed set of the source LSP. On a violation, set `reg0[1]=1` and `next` so that the downstream stages (ND, then the final L2 gate) drop the packet. When the LSP has an empty `port_security=[]`, the stage is bypassed (the priority 0 default action is `next`).

**Why it exists.** OpenStack Neutron security requires that a VM cannot spoof the source IP of another VM on the same subnet. Before OVN, the Neutron OVS agent used per-VM iptables `-m mac` rules to enforce this, which was complex and slow to sync. OVN moves the check into the declarative pipeline.

**Problems it solves.** (a) prevent a VM from sending packets with a fake IP to bypass source-IP-based ACLs, (b) prevent L3-level ARP poisoning (the dedicated `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_ND` stage handles ARP and NDP), (c) form the foundation for stateful ACLs to recognise the real source.

**Importance.** Peripheral in complexity but foundational for security. Multi-tenant data centres must enable it. A single-tenant lab can disable it with `port_security=[]`.

**Mechanism.** Flow generation at v22.03.8 is in `build_lswitch_input_port_sec_op` (`northd/northd.c:5615`); the IP-specific logic is one branch within that function (the `_ip` suffix split into a separate function happened in branch-24.03+). The function iterates over each LSP carrying IPv4 or IPv6 entries in `port_security` and emits a high-priority flow matching `inport == "<lsp>" && eth.src == <mac> && (ip4.src == <ip> || ip4.src == 0.0.0.0)` with action `next;`. A lower-priority flow at priority 95 matches `inport == "<lsp>" && (ip || ip6)` with action `reg0[1] = 1; next;` to catch violators. IPv4 permits `0.0.0.0` so DHCPDISCOVER still passes; IPv6 permits the unspecified `::` for ND solicitation per RFC 4861. Example flow on an LS where LSP `lsp-vm1` has `port_security="aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 10.0.0.5"`:

```
table=9 (ls_in_port_sec_ip), priority=90,
  match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 &&
         (ip4.src == 10.0.0.5 || ip4.src == 0.0.0.0)),
  action=(next;)
table=9, priority=80,
  match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 && ip),
  action=(reg0[1] = 1; next;)
table=9, priority=0, match=(1), action=(next;)
```

**How an operator masters this.** Read `port_security` on the LSP with `ovn-nbctl get Logical_Switch_Port lsp-vm1 port_security`; verify the stage 9 flow for that LSP with `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_in_port_sec_ip`; debug a spoof attempt with `ovn-trace` using a fake source IP, the trace reports `reg0[1]=1` set at stage 1.

**Classification.** Pipeline ingress security gate. Same family as `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` (L2 MAC) and `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_ND` (ARP and NDP). Symmetric counterpart of `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_IP` on egress (which verifies the destination IP).

**Usage workflow.** (1) Create the LSP with `lsp-set-port-security-addresses lsp-vm1 "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 10.0.0.5"`. (2) Verify that the stage 9 flow is generated automatically. (3) Test a spoof attempt by sending a raw-socket packet with source 10.0.0.99 from the VM; the packet is dropped at the final L2 stage after `reg0[1]=1` is set.

**When something goes wrong.** Symptom: a freshly booted VM completes DHCP cleanly, but once it has an IP, traffic does not leave (drop at table 8). Common cause: `port_security` is configured with the MAC only and no IP, so a valid `ip4.src=10.0.0.5` packet still matches the priority 80 catch-all and `reg0[1]=1` is set, leading to a drop. Fix: add the IP to `port_security`.

**Tightly related to.** `Logical_Switch_Port.port_security` (the configuration trigger), `REGBIT_PORT_SEC_DROP=reg0[1]` (the deferred drop), `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` (the final gate), `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_ND` (ND sibling). Loosely coupled: stateful ACL (only packets that pass port-security reach ACL evaluation).

**Version differences.** OVN 2.4 to 20.03: combined into stage 0. OVN 20.06: split into three stages. OVN 22.03 (the curriculum baseline): stable. OVN 24.03: no semantic change, just compile-time optimisation when an LSP has many IPs.

**Observation and verification.**

```
$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_in_port_sec_ip
  table=1 (ls_in_port_sec_ip), priority=90,
    match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 &&
           (ip4.src == 10.0.0.5 || ip4.src == 0.0.0.0)), action=(next;)
  table=1, priority=80,
    match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 && ip),
    action=(reg0[1] = 1; next;)
```

**Source code reference.** `northd/northd.c` function `build_lswitch_input_port_security_ip()` (branch-22.03). Stage token `S_SWITCH_IN_PORT_SEC_IP` defined in `northd/lflow.h` (logical table 1, OF table 9). The `reg0[1]=1` action is parsed in `lib/actions.c`.

**Real-world incident.** Q1 2025, OpenStack-on-OVN cluster: a tenant VM received its IP through DHCP but then could not ping the gateway. `ovn-trace` reported the packet drop at table 8 because `reg0[1]=1`. Root cause: Nova allocated the IP through IPAM but the port `addresses` were not synced into `port_security` (a race in the Neutron OVN driver). Fix: re-run `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security-addresses` for each affected LSP; the downstream Neutron driver patch makes the sync atomic.

**Synthetic exercise.**

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-add ls-psec
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-psec lsp-vm1
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-vm1 "aa:11:11:11:11:11 10.0.0.5"
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-vm1 "aa:11:11:11:11:11 10.0.0.5"
# Lab task 1: ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-psec | grep ls_in_port_sec_ip should show three priorities (90, 80, 0).
# Lab task 2: ovn-trace with ip4.src=10.0.0.5 should pass (reg0[1]=0).
# Lab task 3: ovn-trace with ip4.src=10.0.0.99 should set reg0[1]=1 and drop at stage 0.
```

**Common failures and diagnostic signals.** (a) `port_security` carries only the MAC, so all IP traffic is still dropped after DHCP. (b) IPv6 traffic fails even though IPv4 works, the operator forgot to add the IPv6 entry to port_security. (c) DHCPDISCOVER is dropped even though the subnet is correct, check that the stage permits `ip4.src == 0.0.0.0` (it does by default).

**Comparison with other systems.** Linux bridge `nft add rule ... iif tap-vmN ip saddr != 10.0.0.5 drop` is analogous per VM. OpenStack Neutron `port_security_enabled=true` is analogous (the legacy implementation used iptables). VMware NSX `Spoofguard` is analogous. Cisco IP Source Guard `ip verify source port-security` is analogous. The OVN distinction: declarative through NBDB, follows VM migration, and `ovn-controller` compiles per-chassis flows onto `br-int` automatically.

---

## §13.19.27 LS_IN_PORT_SEC_ND, block L2.5 ARP and NDP spoofing

**Concept.** `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_ND` is logical stage **number 2** of LS ingress, immediately after `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_IP`. The stage specifically checks **ARP request and reply** (IPv4) and **IPv6 Neighbor Discovery Solicitation and Advertisement** (NS and NA), and defers a drop through `REGBIT_PORT_SEC_DROP` when an LSP sends ARP or NDP with `arp.sha`, `nd.sll`, or `nd.tll` not matching the port_security MAC, or with `arp.spa` or `nd.target` not matching an allowed IP. Type: **pipeline ingress security gate**, subtype "L2.5 ARP and NDP filter peripheral".

**History and background.** The stage was split out in the same OVN 20.06 (2020) wave that divided port-security into three stages. Before OVN 20.06, ARP spoofing was not blocked at the pipeline; the operator had to use host iptables or ebtables. OVN 21.03 extended the coverage to full IPv6 NDP.

**Position in the architecture.** Logical stage 2 in LS_IN, OF table 10 (per Part 13.16 line 153). It sits after the IP filter (table 9) and before `LS_IN_LOOKUP_FDB` (table 11). Scope: only ARP packets (`arp`) and IPv6 ND packets (`nd_ns` and `nd_na`).

**Role.** Verify that every ARP packet coming from an LSP carries `arp.sha` (sender hardware address) matching the configured `eth.src` and `arp.spa` (sender protocol address) matching one of the IPv4 addresses in `port_security`. Similarly for NDP: `nd.sll` (source link-layer address) must match `eth.src`, and `nd.target` must match an IPv6 address (for NA) or be unrestricted (for NS with source `::`).

**Why it exists.** ARP spoofing is the classic attack vector: a VM sends a gratuitous ARP with sender IP equal to the gateway IP and MAC equal to the attacker's MAC, so every other VM on the LS updates its MAC binding incorrectly and traffic to the gateway is redirected. A pipeline-level filter eliminates this vector declaratively.

**Problems it solves.** (a) gratuitous ARP poisoning, (b) NDP RA spoofing in IPv6, (c) NS with a target IP that does not belong to the LSP, (d) self-inconsistent declarations in the `eth.src` and `arp.sha` pair.

**Importance.** Peripheral in complexity, medium in security weight. Multi-tenant data centres especially need it. Public cloud deployments require it.

**How it works.** Flow generation function: `build_lswitch_input_port_security_nd()` in `northd/northd.c` (verified on branch-22.03). The function emits a pair of flows per LSP: a high-priority match for the legitimate case `(arp.sha == <mac> && arp.spa == <ip>)` with action `next;`, and a low-priority catch-all match `(arp || nd)` with action `reg0[1] = 1; next;`. IPv6 NS with the unspecified source is also allowed (per RFC 4861) through a separate sub-flow. Example on an LSP `lsp-vm1` configured with MAC `aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01` and IP `10.0.0.5`:

```
table=10 (ls_in_port_sec_nd), priority=90,
  match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 &&
         arp.sha == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 && arp.spa == 10.0.0.5),
  action=(next;)
table=10, priority=80,
  match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && (arp || nd)),
  action=(reg0[1] = 1; next;)
table=10, priority=0, match=(1), action=(next;)
```

**How an operator masters this.** When a VM cannot see the gateway after DHCP completes, check whether the VM sends a gratuitous ARP (`tcpdump` on the tap), whether `port_security` carries the VM's IP, and whether stage 10 has the priority 90 flow for that LSP. When ARP poisoning is suspected, dump the `MAC_Binding` table and look for an unfamiliar MAC bound to the gateway IP.

**Classification.** ARP and NDP security gate stage. Same family as `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` and `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_IP`. Different from `LS_IN_ARP_ND_RSP` (stage 26): `ARP_ND_RSP` acts as a responder on behalf of the router or switch, whereas `PORT_SEC_ND` is an anti-spoof filter.

**Usage workflow.** (1) Run `lsp-set-port-security-addresses` to set the MAC and IP. (2) Verify the stage 10 flow for the LSP. (3) Test a gratuitous ARP with a fake IP from the VM; the packet is dropped at stage 0 because `reg0[1]=1`.

**When something goes wrong.** If the VM does not receive the ARP reply from the gateway, the VM may have sent an ARP request with `arp.spa` outside `port_security`, which causes the drop. Alternatively, an IPv6 NDP NS with a target IP outside the allowed set means the NA never arrives.

**Tightly related to.** `Logical_Switch_Port.port_security`, `REGBIT_PORT_SEC_DROP=reg0[1]`, `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` and `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_IP` (siblings), `MAC_Binding` (downstream impact if spoofing is allowed). Loosely coupled: `LS_IN_ARP_ND_RSP` (the native ARP responder).

**Version differences.** OVN 20.06: introduced. OVN 21.03: extended to full IPv6 NDP (NS with source `::`). OVN 22.03: stable. OVN 23.06: added ND Router Solicitation support for IPv6 SLAAC (allows RS with source `::`).

**Observation and verification.**

```
$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_in_port_sec_nd
  table=2 (ls_in_port_sec_nd), priority=90,
    match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 &&
           arp.sha == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 && arp.spa == 10.0.0.5), action=(next;)

$ ovn-trace ls1 'inport=="lsp-vm1" && eth.src==aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 && eth.dst==ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff && arp.spa==10.0.0.99 && arp.tpa==10.0.0.1 && arp.op==1'
  ingress(dp="ls1", inport="lsp-vm1")
   2. ls_in_port_sec_nd (priority 80): reg0[1] = 1; next;
   ...
   0. ls_in_port_sec_l2 (priority 50): drop;  // deferred
```

**Source code reference.** `northd/northd.c` function `build_lswitch_input_port_security_nd()` (branch-22.03). Stage token `S_SWITCH_IN_PORT_SEC_ND` (logical table 2, OF table 10). The NB schema `Logical_Switch_Port.port_security` is documented in `ovn-nb.xml` under port_security (verified: IPv6 ND solicitation allows the unspecified address).

**Real-world incident.** Q4 2024, OVN 22.03 deployment: a pen-tester ran `arpspoof` from a tenant VM to impersonate the gateway IP. In a normal Linux bridge setup ARP poisoning would have succeeded immediately, but OVN dropped every ARP packet with the wrong `arp.spa`. The pen-test report: the cluster passed the ARP poisoning test. Verified through `ovn-trace`, which showed `reg0[1]=1`.

**Synthetic exercise.**

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-vm1 "aa:11:11:11:11:11 10.0.0.5"
# Lab task 1: ovn-trace gratuitous ARP with arp.spa==10.0.0.5 should pass.
# Lab task 2: ovn-trace with arp.spa==10.0.0.99 should set reg0[1]=1 and drop.
# Lab task 3: ovn-trace IPv6 NS with nd.target==fe80::1, src=:: should pass (unspecified allowed).
# Lab task 4: arping -U 10.0.0.99 -I eth0 from a real VM, tcpdump on the tap shows the packet leaving but no reply arriving.
```

**Common failures and diagnostic signals.** (a) IPv6 SLAAC fails to obtain the prefix, check whether ND RS is dropped at stage 2 (this requires OVN 23.06 or later). (b) A VM that performs an ARP probe (RFC 5227, source IP `0.0.0.0`) is dropped, verify that the stage allows `arp.spa=0.0.0.0` (OVN allows it). (c) Gratuitous ARP from a freshly booted VM does not update `MAC_Binding` on other chassis, check whether `port_security` already carries the IP.

**Comparison with other systems.** Linux `arptables -A INPUT --src-mac ... --src-ip ... -j ACCEPT` is analogous. Cisco `ip arp inspection` (DAI) is analogous and uses the DHCP snooping binding table. NSX-T DFW has dedicated rules for ARP. The OVN distinction: integrated into the declarative pipeline through the `port_security` field, no DHCP snooping required because `port_security` is filled by IPAM when the VM is created.

---

## §13.19.28 LS_IN_LOOKUP_FDB, look up the MAC in the cluster-wide FDB table

**Concept.** `LS_IN_LOOKUP_FDB` is logical stage **number 3** of LS ingress and is dedicated to **looking up the source MAC** of the packet in the `FDB` table (SBDB) to determine which port on the cluster has learned that MAC. The stage applies only to LSPs with `addresses="unknown"` or empty port_security (router peering LSPs, VLAN trunks, external gateways). When the MAC is not yet in the FDB, the downstream `LS_IN_PUT_FDB` stage learns it. Type: **pipeline FDB lookup peripheral**, subtype "MAC learning lookup gate".

**History and background.** The stage was introduced in OVN 22.03 (early 2022) when Numan Siddique (Red Hat) moved L2 learning from per-chassis OVS bridge native learning to the cluster-wide SBDB FDB table. Before OVN 22.03, each chassis learned MACs independently through the OVS bridge, which created asymmetry. The `LOOKUP_FDB` and `PUT_FDB` stages were added together with the SBDB `FDB` table (see Part 13.5 §13.5.1c.4).

**Position in the architecture.** Logical stage 3 in LS_IN, OF table 11 (per Part 13.16 line 154). It sits after port-security (tables 8 to 10) and before `LS_IN_PUT_FDB` (table 12). It depends on the SBDB `FDB` table populated by `controller/pinctrl.c`.

**Role.** Call the `lookup_fdb(P, A)` action to look up `(datapath, eth.src)` in the FDB. On a hit, set `REGBIT_LKUP_FDB=1` (`reg0[11]`); the next stage `PUT_FDB` then skips the insert. On a miss, `REGBIT_LKUP_FDB=0`, and `PUT_FDB` inserts a new entry.

**Why it exists.** The pre-22.03 design (OVS bridge native learning) had a problem: chassis A learned MAC X on port P; chassis B had not yet seen traffic from X, so it did not know where X lived and flooded every packet aimed at X, wasting bandwidth. A cluster-wide FDB through SBDB lets every chassis read the same data and all know where X lives.

**Problems it solves.** (a) flood storm when the cluster has just booted (nothing learned yet), (b) asymmetric MAC learning between chassis, (c) the migration learning gap when a VM moves to a new chassis.

**Importance.** Peripheral for a pure-VM LS (because LSPs have explicit `addresses`, no FDB is needed). Medium importance for an LS with many LSPs of `addresses=unknown` (router peering, VLAN trunks, external gateways).

**How it works.** Flow generation function: `build_lswitch_lookup_fdb()` in `northd/northd.c` (verified on branch-22.03). The function emits a flow only when the LS has at least one LSP with `addresses=unknown`. The priority 100 flow for an unknown LSP is `match=(inport == "lsp-router-peer")` with action `reg0[11] = lookup_fdb(inport, eth.src); next;`. The priority 0 default action is `next`. The `lookup_fdb` action is parsed in `lib/actions.c` and executed at runtime by `controller/pinctrl.c` function `pinctrl_handle_lookup_fdb()`.

```
table=11 (ls_in_lookup_fdb), priority=100,
  match=(inport == "lsp-router-peer"),
  action=(reg0[11] = lookup_fdb(inport, eth.src); next;)
table=11, priority=0, match=(1), action=(next;)
```

**How an operator masters this.** Understand when the stage is active: only LSes that have at least one LSP with `addresses=unknown`. Verify the FDB table with `ovn-sbctl --columns=mac,dp_key,port_key list FDB`. Debug "a freshly migrated VM floods traffic" by checking the FDB before and after migration.

**Classification.** Pipeline FDB stage. Same family as `LS_IN_PUT_FDB` (the lookup-then-learn pair). Different from `MAC_Binding` (the LR ARP cache): FDB is for L2 learning whereas `MAC_Binding` is for L3 ARP and NDP resolution.

**Usage workflow.** (1) Create an LSP with `addresses=unknown` (for example, a router peering port). (2) Verify that stage 11 emits a flow for that LSP. (3) Send a packet from an unknown MAC; `ovn-trace` shows `lookup_fdb()` returning 0 and `reg0[11]=0`. (4) The `PUT_FDB` stage inserts the entry. (5) The next time the same MAC arrives, the lookup hits and `reg0[11]=1`.

**When something goes wrong.** Symptom: MAC traffic keeps flooding without converging. Possible causes: (a) `ovn-controller` cannot insert into the FDB due to OVSDB permissions, (b) the FDB row carries a stale `port_key` (the LSP was deleted), so the lookup hits but forwards to the wrong port, (c) `other_config:fdb_age_threshold` is too short, so entries expire before they are reused.

**Tightly related to.** The `FDB` table (SBDB), the `lookup_fdb` action, `LS_IN_PUT_FDB` (sister), `REGBIT_LKUP_FDB=reg0[11]`, and `Logical_Switch_Port.addresses=unknown`. See Part 13.5 §13.5.1c.4 for the FDB schema. Loosely coupled: `MAC_Binding` (L3 sibling) and OVS bridge native learning (an alternative path when FDB is disabled).

**Version differences.** OVN before 22.03: no FDB stage; per-chassis OVS bridge learning is used. OVN 22.03: introduces the `FDB` SBDB table and the stage pair. OVN 23.06: adds `Logical_Switch.other_config:fdb_age_threshold` (default 0 means no expiration). OVN 24.09: `ovn-controller` supports the `MAX_FDB_ENTRIES` limit (commit `fb96ae3679`, `controller/pinctrl.c`).

**Cách quan sát + xác minh.**

```
$ ovn-sbctl --columns=mac,dp_key,port_key list FDB
  mac      : "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:09"
  dp_key   : 5
  port_key : 8

$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-with-trunk | grep ls_in_lookup_fdb
  table=3 (ls_in_lookup_fdb), priority=100,
    match=(inport == "lsp-trunk"),
    action=(reg0[11] = lookup_fdb(inport, eth.src); next;)

$ ovn-trace ls1 'inport=="lsp-trunk" && eth.src==aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:09 && ...'
  3. ls_in_lookup_fdb (priority 100): reg0[11] = lookup_fdb(...); next;
```

**Source code reference.** `northd/northd.c` function `build_lswitch_lookup_fdb()` (branch-22.03). Action implementation: `lib/actions.c` parses `lookup_fdb`. Runtime: `controller/pinctrl.c` `pinctrl_handle_lookup_fdb()`. Stage token `S_SWITCH_IN_LOOKUP_FDB` (logical table 3, OF table 11). SBDB schema: `ovn-sb.ovsschema` table `FDB`. OF table `OFTABLE_LOOKUP_FDB=72` in `controller/lflow.h` (see Part 13.16 line 64).

**Real-world incident.** Q3 2024, OVN 22.03 cluster with 200 VLAN trunk LSPs: traffic between router peerings kept flooding without converging after 30 minutes. Investigation: `ovn-sbctl list FDB | wc -l` reported 0 entries. Root cause: `ovn-controller` was in a crash loop on one chassis and could not insert into the FDB. Fix: restart the controller; the FDB populated within a few seconds. Lesson learned: monitor the FDB row count as a health check.

**Synthetic exercise.**

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-add ls-trunk
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-trunk lsp-trunk-A
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-trunk-A unknown
# Lab task 1: ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-trunk | grep ls_in_lookup_fdb shows the priority 100 flow for lsp-trunk-A.
# Lab task 2: send traffic from a new MAC through lsp-trunk-A; ovn-sbctl list FDB shows a new entry.
# Lab task 3: repeat the traffic; ovn-trace reports lookup_fdb hit and reg0[11]=1.
# Lab task 4: set fdb_age_threshold=10, wait 15 seconds; the entry expires and the lookup misses.
```

**Common failures and diagnostic signals.** (a) FDB does not populate even though the unknown LSP is set up; check whether the `ovn-controller` log shows `pinctrl_handle_lookup_fdb` activity. (b) A stale FDB entry forwards to the wrong port; clean up manually with `ovn-sbctl destroy FDB <uuid>`. (c) A cluster with more than 10,000 unknown LSPs hits FDB scale issues; enable `MAX_FDB_ENTRIES` (24.09 and later) or shard the LS.

**Comparison with other systems.** Linux bridge `bridge fdb show` is analogous (per-host learning). Cisco Nexus VXLAN EVPN with BGP-EVPN MAC route announcements is analogous (cluster-wide learning through a control plane). The Open vSwitch `mac-learning` module is analogous (per-bridge learning). The OVN distinction: cluster-wide through SBDB, no BGP needed, no separate control protocol needed.

---

## §13.19.29 LS_IN_PUT_FDB, learn a new MAC into the cluster-wide FDB table

**Concept.** `LS_IN_PUT_FDB` is logical stage **number 4** of LS ingress and is dedicated to **inserting or updating** an FDB entry when `LS_IN_LOOKUP_FDB` missed (`REGBIT_LKUP_FDB=0`). The stage calls the `put_fdb(P, A)` action to push `(datapath, eth.src) -> inport` to `ovn-controller` through a controller action; `controller/pinctrl.c` then performs the SBDB `FDB` insert. Type: **pipeline FDB learning peripheral**, subtype "MAC learning insert step".

**History and background.** The stage was introduced together with `LS_IN_LOOKUP_FDB` in OVN 22.03 (early 2022) as the learning pair. Before OVN 22.03, learning happened implicitly through OVS bridge native learning; OVN 22.03 converted it into an explicit pipeline action.

**Position in the architecture.** Logical stage 4 in LS_IN, OF table 12 (per Part 13.16 line 155). It sits after `LOOKUP_FDB` (table 11) and before `LS_IN_PRE_ACL` (table 13).

**Role.** When `reg0[11]=0` (lookup miss), the stage calls `put_fdb(inport, eth.src)` and the `ovn-controller` upcall handler inserts a row into the SBDB FDB. When `reg0[11]=1` (already present), the stage is skipped.

**Why it exists.** Splitting lookup and learning into two stages lets the REGBIT serve as an intermediate flag, which avoids duplicate inserts and learns only when necessary. The check-then-act pattern matches `LS_IN_DHCP_OPTIONS` and `LS_IN_DHCP_RESPONSE`.

**Problems it solves.** (a) idempotent insert (only on a miss), (b) async insert through a controller action does not block the fast path, (c) the per-chassis controller updates SBDB so other chassis read the entry immediately.

**Importance.** Same tier as `LOOKUP_FDB`. Peripheral for a pure-VM LS, medium for trunk and peering LSes.

**How it works.** Flow generation function: `build_lswitch_put_fdb()` in `northd/northd.c` (verified on branch-22.03). The function emits flows only for LSPs with `addresses=unknown`:

```
table=12 (ls_in_put_fdb), priority=100,
  match=(reg0[11] == 0 && inport == "lsp-router-peer"),
  action=(put_fdb(inport, eth.src); next;)
table=12, priority=0, match=(1), action=(next;)
```

The `put_fdb` action is a **controller action** (like `put_arp` and `put_dhcp_opts`): the packet is upcalled to `ovn-controller`, the handler inserts the SBDB row, and the packet is not blocked (it continues the pipeline immediately). The controller deduplicates by checking whether `(dp_key, mac)` already exists before inserting.

**How an operator masters this.** Understand that `put_fdb` is a controller action and therefore carries upcall overhead. Each new MAC causes one upcall. When the cluster has high MAC churn (for example, many ephemeral VMs), the FDB grows large and the upcall rate is high. Sizing: monitor the `ovn-controller` log and the SBDB transaction rate.

**Classification.** Pipeline FDB learning stage. Sister of `LOOKUP_FDB`. Different from `put_arp` (LR `MAC_Binding` learning): `put_fdb` is for L2 forwarding, `put_arp` is for L3 ARP resolution.

**Usage workflow.** (1) Configure the LSP with `addresses=unknown`. (2) Send traffic from a new MAC. (3) `ovn-sbctl list FDB` shows the new entry after roughly a few tens of milliseconds. (4) The next time the same MAC arrives, the lookup hits and `put` is skipped.

**When something goes wrong.** Symptom: the FDB does not grow even though traffic flows through. Causes: (a) `ovn-controller` upcall bottleneck (CPU, raft latency), (b) `pinctrl.c` rate limit, (c) SBDB transaction conflict that forces insert retries. Diagnose with the `ovn-controller` log and the SBDB transaction log.

**Tightly related to.** The `put_fdb` action, the `FDB` table, `LS_IN_LOOKUP_FDB` (sister), `REGBIT_LKUP_FDB`, and `controller/pinctrl.c` function `pinctrl_handle_put_fdb()`. See Part 13.5 §13.5.1c.4. Loosely coupled: the `put_arp` action (the LR analogue).

**Version differences.** OVN before 22.03: not present. OVN 22.03: introduced with the FDB table. OVN 23.06: adds the `fdb_age_threshold` configuration (auto-aging rows). OVN 24.09: supports the `MAX_FDB_ENTRIES` limit to prevent unbounded FDB growth (upstream commit `fb96ae3679` in `controller/pinctrl.c`, the `MAX_FDB_ENTRIES` section).

**Cách quan sát + xác minh.**

```
$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_in_put_fdb
  table=4 (ls_in_put_fdb), priority=100,
    match=(reg0[11] == 0 && inport == "lsp-trunk-A"),
    action=(put_fdb(inport, eth.src); next;)

$ ovn-sbctl --columns=mac,dp_key,port_key list FDB
```
